<Author>1bob
<Content>Average Booking through Hotwire, I expected a less desirable room and that's what I got. The rooms on the 3rd floor are fairly small and do not have balconies or views. The room was very clean however, and everything was in working order. The free wired internet was fantastic and much better than the wi-fi you normally find in hotels. The free safe, refrig, microwave, coffee maker, coffee, newspaper, LCD TV,etc. made up for the room. Although the hotel was renovated a few years ago somehow they managed to retain the shabby appearance. The room furnishings were disproportionately large for the size of the room and featured lots of drawers and shelves but not a desk nor writing area and not even a chair! Yes, they have a bowl of apples at the front desk and give you bottles of cold water upon check-in. Most of the staff was extremely nice although the person who checked me in (Ms. Sina) was efficient and professional but lacked the aloha spiriti. All in all, this is a good choice if you're looking for a budget hotel.

<Author>Jodellefitzh20
<Content>Aqua Aloha had me at hello... My girlfriend and I had our girlfriend getaway week at the Aqua Aloha Surf and Spa and it was great! Upon check-in the apples and the water are a welcome treat, the bar always had football on for me to check the scores of my Chicago Bears (Go Bears!), the free continental breakfast was swell, the free newspaper was a welcome treat to read at the beach daily, the room was small but cozy and very clean, the beds were comfy, the staff was friendly and helpful, and the beach and shopping and dining is all a quick walk away. Now, for fine print: if you want to pay $20 a day to park here, go ahead, but if you drive around the block slowly a few times you can find FREE parking along the sides of the road. All along Ala Wai street which is the street that backs up to the hotel has free parking everyday all day long if you can find a spot. Just drive slow and stalk people who look like they are walking to their cars! We never paid for parking all 5 days we were there! Then once there, walk next door to the food pantry and buy some lunch stuff that you can make your lunch each day, and that way you get breakfast for free, pack a picnic lunch for the beach, and dinner will be the only meal you have to pay for! You can do Hawaii on a budget you just have to be smart about it. Speaking of eating: YOU HAVE TO EAT AT THE YARDHOUSE FOR DINNER ONE NIGHT! IT'S SOME OF THE BEST FOOD I'VE EVER EATEN. Most important: if you are only planning on staying in honolulu and waikiki you are missing the real Hawaii. Take a trip less than an hour away up to North Shore and experience paradise at Waimea Bay - it's awe-inspiring. Enjoy all that Hawaii has to offer and breathe in the smell of fresh plumerias!

<Author>ellysan1
<Content>Great 5-Star Old Hawaii Hospitality Gem That's A Super Bargain Last month we went to Hawaii for the first time for our daughter's Wedding. We needed an inexpensive place to stay several days before all the guests showed up for the Wedding hotel. I read about all the Aqua Boutique Hotels on-line and read the various reviews. When I found an incredible deal for the Aloha Surf, centrally located near the beach, that included free high speed Internet and continental breakfast, I couldn't pass it up. When my daughter heard about the deal, she had me book her a room too. That really put pressure on me since she lives in Japan. So, when we arrived at the Aloha Surf we were totally shocked that it was not rated as a 5-Star Hotel.It was super, super clean. The lobby was understated and beautiful. The staff could not do enough for us. They made you feel that you were a guest in their home and not a wallet to extract every cent. The room had everything that was advertised including a private lanai.I would have liked a desk in the room which would have made it more convenient for me to work. I needed an Ethernet cable to connect. The front desk simply handed it to me and asked if there was anything else I needed. The continental breakfast was better than most and was a great way to start the day without a hassle or an expense. Parking in their lot was convenient and less expensive than other hotels. My daughter was very pleased with everything at the Aloha Surf. Our biggest regret was that we had to leave the Aloha Surf and move to the clip joint down the block that was the wedding hotel. Anyone who is looking for more bang for their buck- and in these times who isn't- should definitely stay at the Aloha Surf  Spa Boutique Hotel. You will have the experience of Old Hawaiian hospitality in a technically up-to-date setting. Mahalo Aloha Surf!

<Author>teamwingnut
<Content>Definitely worth more than I paid for I'd read prior reviews about this property, and felt a bit of trepidation and what I might encounter during my stay. It turned out my anxiety was groundless...The Pros: 1) Located in the heart of Waikiki, within walking distance to a LOT. 2) The bellhop was quick to offer his assistance. 3) The front desk staffer had us checked in within minutes; the complimentary bottles of water on check-in and the free apples were a really nice touch. 4) The hotel's a bit on the small side, but the elevator is centrally located, so the walk, even from the basement parking spots to the room, wasn't that far. 5) Though on the small side, the room was clean and well-appointed; the sofa, microwave, refrigerator, dishes and eating utensils made it feel like a junior suite. We were able to save some money on food by purchasing microwaveable meals or bringing back leftovers to reheat later. 6) The queen and twin beds and the sofa would sleep four adults easily (though there were only two of us during our stay). 7) Free internet (see cons below as well). 8) Our housekeeper was friendly and efficient. 9) When we had a problem with our TV remote, we mentioned it to a passing maintenance worker and he fixed the problem within 10 minutes. 10) When we had a problem with our neighbors smoking on their balcony (see cons below), one call to the front desk resolved the situation.The Cons: 1) The (lack of) parking--Waikiki parking in general is a nightmare; had I not called ahead and reserved one of the hotel's parking spaces, I'd have had to resort to street parking or finding a lot. At the tune of $20 a day, the parking was a bit pricey, but it was worth not having to worry about trying to find parking, and the walk to the room was short. 2) The window-unit air conditioner was a bit lacking in performance, especially since our room faced the west, and heated up during the afternoon. 3) Though the hotel is a non-smoking property, the couple in the next room, upwind from us, were out on their balcony puffing away. I called the front desk and was told that clients were told they could smoke on their balconies as long as they kept the smoke from going back into their room. The smoke from that couple was making its way into our room through the glass-louver windows and exacerbating my friend's asthma. One call to the front desk fixed the problem, though (see pros above). 4) Internet access was wireless only in the lobby and by the pool. In the room, internet access was wired, and the cable provided by the front desk were a bit short, which turned our room into a kind of steeple-chase arrangement, with us stepping over the cable to get around the room.Obviously, the pros FAR outweighed the cons, and I'd definitely recommend this property.  
<Date>Oct 26, 2008

Very annoying, as it made it difficult to get to the lamp and the alarm clock (which wasn't even plugged in.) The curtain was anchored both on the ceiling AND the floor, so there was NO moving it whatsoever. Have no idea what it was there for.At least there was a fridge and a safe. The fridge was small, but adequate. The safe was fairly old, but did the job. It was locked with a key which we had to take with us anytime we were out of the room.The size of the room really didn't bother me--though it was very small--since we spent only time sleeping in it. (After all, if you want to spend your time in Hawaii in your room, why go?) The room service was okay. The bed was made every day, though the glasses that were provided were not replaced very often. The best part of the room, however, was the balcony. There was, unfortunately, very little view of the ocean. Just mainly the city. However, the cool breeze did make it decent.The hotel was about a block or two from the ocean, so it was pretty easy to get to.The staff in the lobby was pretty friendly, though one manager had told us that the elevators were turned off at 6:30pm every night 'for security'. That, to me, was pretty stupid. There are locks on every door, accessed only by an electronic room key. However, except for that first night, we never saw that manager again and the elevator worked past 6:30 the rest of the time.The breakfast wasn't great, but it also wasn't bad. At least it saved money having to buy breakfast every day. Showing our room key wasn't a big deal for us. After all, they had to make sure that not just anyone could access it. Also, except for the first day, we never had to show our room key again when going to breakfast. We had toast, biscuits, fruit (pineapple, apples and just once--oranges). Plus juice and coffee. Not a bad breakfast.We didn't notice any bugs at all.Parking, however, was a different story. I know there is a lack of space, but THIS was ridiculous. Parking downstairs, it took two of us to park the car, because there was VERY little space to maneuver. Do NOT bring anything bigger than a compact car down here, or you will be in trouble!There was another parking lot at ground level and we were told that if all the spaces were used up, to let them know and they would get us a spot. They have some spots blocked off and reserved just for this. They guarantee a spot for you. Maybe not a great spot, but they guarantee you a spot.Doubt we would rebook at this hotel, though. There were just too many annoyances to make us go back. If you want cheap, this is that, but not really a lot to recommend it much. BEWARE THE BED!!!  
<Date>Oct 23, 2008

<Author>AzFlyMom
<Content>Best Budget Hotel I have ever stayed in So happy to find this hotel located in the center of Waikiki. I have stayed in about 10 different hotels in Waikiki over the years and this was the best buy. The rooms were decorated nicely. Furniture and tub needed updating but this is a budget hotel. Updating things raises the prices usually. Everything was clean. Staff was very nice. Breakfast good although only open one hour. Lobby, breakfast area, pool, exercise equipment nicer than you would find at a normal budget hotel. Complaints about noise are ridiculous. You are in the middle of Waikiki....all hotels hear the same noise of garbage trucks, parties etc. If you wantt a quiet location, don't stay in Waikiki. I am a flight attendant and stay in hotels all over so I know what is out there and recognize a good deal. I will stay here next visit and will feel lucky if a room is available for the price I paid.

<Author>heids88
<Content>Great hotel but noisy We stayed in this hotel in August at the start of a big trip around the world. Check in is generally not until 3pm but we managed to get in just after 2pm. The complimentary bottles of water provided at that point were a nice touch. Our room was located on the 7th floor, on the same side as the hotel entrance, facing the street. There are two lifts, and generally, we never had to wait long for a lift. The rooms were clean, and tidied every day (although the sheets are not automatically changed every day). There is free internet access in the rooms (reception can loan you a cable) or free Wi-Fi in certain parts of the hotel. Phone calls to local and toll free numbers are free from your room phone. The rooms are air conditioned, have coffee making facilities, a bar fridge, safe, bathrobes, and bath products. The hotel is also conveniently located near ABC Stores (like 7-11 but with clothes etc) and Food Pantry (supermarket), and is close to Waikiki Beach and the shops. The continental breakfast (muffins, fruit, juice, coffee, toast, croissants) was more than adequate. The only thing I can really fault about this hotel is that the rooms are not soundproof, and the windows are just glass louvers, so the noise comes straight in. You can hear people talking outside your room (although this wasn't a big issue), as well as the traffic on the road (this was more the issue). Noise from the traffic continues through the night (although eases a little) and construction work started early (around 5-ish) so you get woken up by sirens, traffic, trucks reversing, etc). Being light sleepers, we had earplugs in and it was still noisy. I'm not sure whether there are 'better' rooms in the hotel for noise, or whether it was because we are light sleepers. Aside from the noise, I would definitely recommend this hotel.

<Author>JennRoberts
<Content>Great hotel Since I'm one of those who loves to read detailed reviews about hotels before I stay in them I figured I have to write one too. I sayed here for a week aug 11-19th with my b/f and the hotel was great. We stayed in the smallest, standard room and it was totally fine. Whoever complains about the size obv. needs more space than really needed. We had more than enuff space for all our luggage and stuff. The only complaint is the small shower. My boyfriend is 62 and had to bend down to wash his hair. Me being 52 had no problem. Fridge came in handy for drinks and stuff we bought. Microwave/ coffee maker were clean didnt use them. Always saw the cleaning crew on our floor so hotel was well kept. Tuesdays they have free drinks in the lobby and free 5 min massages.Breakfast: Toast (whole wheat  white), mini bagels, cream cheese, butter, 3 types of muffins (butterloaf is the best, also had chocolate and blueberry), fruit (pineapple, bananas or oranges and always apples), coffee, tea, juice, oatmeal.Location: Main strip is Kalakaua Ave which is where Moana Surfrider (very $$$ hotel)  Outrigger are located. Aloha Surf was only a couple blocks away, maybe a 5 mins walk. So you know this was a great location. Right by the beach, restaraunts , stores (gucci, prada, fendi, louis vutton, juicy, rolex...) Bus stop is right at the corner of Aloha Surf (Kuhio ave). A tip if you're planning on taking the bus is print out the time tables b/c they're not listed at the stop. Just go to www.thebus.org and it even tells you what buses to take to popular locations. Shuttles are always available thru the hotel and flyers/attraction booklets which are more $ than the $2 bus sometimes worth it minus the hassle of waiting for the bus and just getting picked up. We personally took the bus to sea life park  Hanauma bay. (22, 23, 42 are popular bus routes for these places including pearl harbor) There are ABC stores every 30 feet literally so if you 4got anything dont worry, its basically like a CVS or Walgreens.Dining: Many local places to eat near by like subway, kfc, cheesecake factory, planet hollywood...hard rock cafe is a 25 mins walk away (1.25 miles) in a kinda run down area so stick to the main strip. Our favorite restuarant is Tiki Bar  Grill. If you go you have to order the edemame and mac encrusted mahi mahi it was so good we ate there 3 outta 8 nights! It's on Kalakaua Ave so its pretty close (10-15min walk). Walk outta the hotel and when u get to Kalakaua make a left n jus go straight til you see it and all the tiki torches. (very pretty at night). All in all it was a great stay, great location, friendly staff were very helpful booking things to do but i would say they dont give any discount since they work thru expedia so if you just look thru attraction booklets or walk in the street people hand out fleyer for cheaper attractions. Def. would stay here again!

<Author>retrovertigo
<Content>Great budget hotel - But not perfect I have to start by saying that due to the nature of my work coupled with my own personal travel, I tend to stay at a fair amount of hotels all over the world. They range anywhere from a 5 star to a private room in a hostel. If something piques my interest, I will give it a try. You never know, I have had great stays at very cheap places and had poor stays at overpriced resorts. I had been reading some about Aqua Resorts and decided to give them a try. The Aqua Aloha had a small suite with a separate bedroom which was perfect for myself, my friend, and her 14 year old daughter. At $169 a night with the fifth night free, not a bad deal. I booked for 5 nights but ended up checking out after 3.I'll start off with the reason for my early departure. I originally had no intention of getting a vehicle. The next day I was speaking with the lady who helps book activities and tours and such. She kept trying to get me to pay for the overpriced transportation that was available for things such as the Polynesian Cultural Center, The Marine Park, Etc. I told her I would just rent a car. No mention whatsoever of any possible problems with parking capacity. Well, after a long day of driving around the island, hitting the Polynesian Cultural Center and the luau and show, we got back around 11 PM and were tired. My friend went in to see how the parking worked and came back out with a map she was given. We were told the garage was full and we would have to park at another property a few blocks away. I wasn't happy about this but tried finding it anyway. After a short while of driving around and not finding it, I came back. I told them this was unacceptable as I didn't book a room at another hotel and I wasn't parking at another hotel. Plus the fact that I didn't feel like walking a 14 year old girl past the hookers and drunken partiers in between. Don't get me wrong, the area is a bit sketchy but I have never felt unsafe there. I just didn't think she needed to see it. Anyway, I was told by the lady at the desk my only other alternative was the pay lot next to the hotel (or street parking of which there was none). I would have to move the car at 7 AM though. So I go over and park, pay the $10, place the receipt on the dash just like the car next to me. The only problem was that the lot is used for 3 purposes. There is restaurant parking and there are spots numbered for the paid parking, which is also available to Food Pantry grocery customers for an hour for free while shopping. I was tired and it is not so clearly marked that you have to watch where you park as even though it is one big lot, not all parking is open. Of course I get up the next morning and the car is gone. And of course I clearly see then the sign where I parked stating it was the restaurant parking. I have since come to find out that this is a common mistake, so I can only believe it is more profitable to tow cars then to put up signs where you pay cautioning people where to park. But, for all of this I can only fault myself and not the hotel in any way. My problem with the hotel is that they advertise on-site parking. They need to add a disclaimer stating: We Do Not Have Near Adequate Enough Parking For The Amount Of People Our Hotel Can Hold And You May Be Required To Park At Another One Of Our Properties Yet Still Be Expected To Pay Full Price But Get A Lovely Late Night Tour Complete With Hookers And Drunk Partiers. Incidentally, even in the parking lot from which I was towed there were a bunch of kids hanging out and getting drunk. I wasn't too concerned for the car as I had rented off of my corporate account which includes the damage waiver. How was I to know they would be the least of my worries?I was pretty annoyed the next morning and promptly checked out after taking a taxi to the tow yard. The staff knew I was irritated and were very good about the whole thing. I expected to end up paying for the entire 5 nights that I booked but was only charged for the 3 that I stayed. I ended up at the Hilton Hawaiian Village for the remaining 2 nights. Unlike a previous reviewer who complained about the Aqua Aloha not being up to her standards then tried to compare the two, a word of advice. You can't try and compare a 5 star resort to a budget hotel. It's like complaining to Ford that your Fiesta doesn't perform like a Porsche. It's apples and oranges and only shows ignorance and arrogance. The reason I went there was that I am a Hilton Honors Diamond member and it was easier to call their reservation desk then spend the morning on the internet or calling different places for a room. Plus I had never stayed there and it looked cool. So, a little about the hotel itself. It does try and come off a bit more upscale then it actually is. It's a decently refurbished older hotel. It is probably one of the nicest budget hotels I have ever stayed in, in the U.S. For the price I paid, the room I was given was excellent. It was big enough for our needs and clean. We had a corner unit on the top floor which gave us a nice sized lanai with a great city view. The only complaint was from the kid saying that the sofa bed was springy and uncomfortable. Quite frankly I don't think I have ever run across a sofa bed that wasn't. Oh, and the ice machine is next to the pool, which really sucks when you are the 16th floor and want ice. Glad we brought t he kid along.The staff was extremely friendly and helpful. I didn't have to deal with them too much, but when I did I was never disappointed (oh yea, except for that whole parking thing). The breakfast was OK. Fruit, pastries, bread, and juice. Nothing to write home about, but filling. I was actually a bit surprised when they asked to see my room key, as I couldn't imagine anyone sneaking into it. We actually only ate there 1 day, and the only bad thing was trying to find a place to sit.Everything said, it is a good value for the money if you are looking to do things on a budget. Clean rooms at a decent price and a friendly, helpful staff. I would never steer anyone away from there. I won't be returning. My ex-wife once said that I could be petty and hold a grudge even when my problems were mostly of my own doing. Guess she was right. Wow, who knew?

<Content>Good Value I booked this place based on reviews here and hotels.com and I basically got what I expected. <Author>CaliforniaGirl22
<Content>Aqua Aloha Surf - Perfect for Me I received a great rate for my room (my family and I had the largest room they have) and it comfortably slept 4 adults and 1 child. Two adults shared a bed, the child slept in the other bed, and two adults shared the couch that pulls out into a bed. Although the beds were not the most comfortable I have ever slept on, you can't expect 700 thread count Egyptian cotton sheets from a modest hotel. My family just needed a place to sleep at night, we had no intention of hanging out in the hotel room. The lanai (balcony) was great for hang drying beach towels, wetsuits, etc. but a little small for much else. We definitely used the kitchen area. Some days we heated up food in the microwave and we made use of the fridge/freezer every day we were there. The bathroom size was as expected for a no frills hotel. The room itself was immaculately clean and the free internet service was terrific! Our maid cleaned the room above and beyond expectations every day we were there. The hotel even gave us a great rate for a hotel room for half the day so we could shower after a day at the beach before we got on our plane home at 10pm. The people at the front desk were more than friendly and helped with anything we needed. The hotel is just a short walk to the beach and has an ABC store at the corner. There was not a noise problem when my family was there, even when the trash truck came for the dumpsters around the back of the hotel. The open lobby was delightful for enjoying a cocktail (the hotel doesn't mind as long as it's in a cup and the free cocktail hour provided by the hotel was very nice. Everyone in my group felt the continental breakfast was the perfect variety of food. They had 3 different juices, various fruits, danishes, muffins, and pastries. It is better than most continental breakfasts at other hotels. There are complaints on here regarding it, but it is important to remember it is a continental breakfast. That doesn't mean a whole spread of eggs, bacon, etc. I would gladly stay here again and probably will unless I can get a better deal or same as deal at a luxury hotel.

<Author>sleonmic
<Content>Great Staff at Aqua Aloha I was sent to Honolulu for a work seminar [lucky me!] and wanted to extend my stay for a few days. I booked the Aqua Aloha Surf through an online agency with a special offer. I found out just before my trip that my company made a mistake on the dates and was off by one day between hotel stays. Of course when you buya promotional offer through an online vendor there is no room for error. You can never reach them to resolve a mistake and they usually will not have the promotional rate any longer. It can be quite costly to fix this sort of mistake. I called the Aqua Aloha Surf directly this time and was very pleased with the service I received. Reservations resolved the problem to my satisfaction. I had some other questions so I called the front desk and spoke with Vinh who was pleasant and helpful. When I had a special request he transferred me to the the manager Jullian. Jullian was great and readily available. I was never given the run around that I have had at other hotels and he was very helpful and considerate. This was my first time using tripadvisor and I learned that some of the negative reviews have to be taken with a grain of salt. Complaints such as noise for example are common to all Waikiki hotels regardless of price. Aqua Aloha gave me options so that I could make my own decision as to what type of room would best suit my needs. I will be coming to Hawaii again soon with an elderly parent and will definately stay at the Aqua Aloha Surf and Spa Hotel as I know they will be attentive to our special needs. The locations is great and I enjoyed my stay Mahalo to the friendly staff and Aloha.

<Author>Aussie_beach_chick
<Content>Great and affordable After reading some of the reviews about this hotel I was a little worried that we would be staying there. But I have to say, I was pleasantly surprised. We were upgraded on check-in to a lovely spacious suite with a very comfortable king sized bed and a balcony with a view of the ocean and the mountains. The room was tastefully decorated and the staff were plesant. Like all buildings in Waikiki, it is on the older side and like alot of the buildings, the room has louvered windows. The hotel is well located, close to a supermarket, bus stops and only a short walk to the beach. We did have a couple of minor issues with the internet in our room and the toilet in the bathroom, but both these were fixed within half an hour of notifying the staff.The breakfast is buffet style, muffins, pastries, toast, fruit and bagels, but this was more than enough to keep us happy.One word of warning, you will get street noise. Having said this, you would get street noise no matter where you stay in Waikiki, it is a noisy place. The hotel is actually down one of the quieter streets you could stay on. I did't get woken once by the noise outside, but if you are a light sleeper, perhaps reconsider your stay in Waikiki.

<Author>eshia01
<Content>Nice place to lay your head.. This budget hotel is good for its price, usually under $100/night. It is centrally located in Waikiki, so you can walk to the beach in about 5 minutes. The rooms are renovated with a modern look, each having a flat screen television. The rooms are a little small, but you're not going to be indoors most of the day anyways. The staff was friendly and helpful. When I checked in to my room. My window faced construction work on the front of hotel. I could literally see the workers walking past my window on their scaffold. When I asked to change my room, they apologized and upgraded me to the deluxe room. If you're going to make reservations, make sure you don't get the side where the constructions at. They will be at it for a couple of months. Parking is $15/day for your car rental, but that is the norm at most hotels. The biggest problem was the air conditioner, which would intermittently buzz loudly. I got use to it, but may bother others.I would definitely stay here again. Its a great deal for what you get. If you're trying to wine and dine a girl/guy or you're on your honeymoon, maybe staying on the beach would be a better choice.

<Author>Dianic
<Content>Nice Hotel for a Great Price We stayed at the Aqua Aloha Surf and Spa for two nights (26-28/4). Due to an early morning flight from Sydney we arrived at the hotel around 10am. Upon check-in we were informed that the room was not ready and to come back around 3pm. As we had signed up to receive the Aqua Resorts newsletter we had a voucher to receive a free upgrade and were given a deluxe partial city view room (we booked a superior room) for $84 per night + tax. We were both given free bottles of water and there were apples at the reception. We came back to the hotel just after 1pm and our room was ready. The room was nice and there was enough space for both of us to put our suitcases. Our room had a queen bed and sofa sleeper and a balcony. We were located on the 8th floor towards the back of the hotel. The room was quiet and both mornings we didn't hear garbage trucks or any other noise. There was a strange noise coming from the shower (sounded like it was in the pipes) but we reported it to the reception on our way out and it was fixed when we returned from dinner. The breakfast in the morning was complimentary and consisted of toast, bagels, jam, cream cheese, pastries, fruit and tea, coffee and juice. We found the breakfast to be filling and quite good. The reception area is nice with plenty of seating and a TV if waiting for a tour or to be picked up to return to the airport. The hotel has a swimming pool which we didn't use. The hotel provided complimentary beach towels so there was no need to bring your own. The front desk staff were friendly and we would be happy to stay here again.

<Author>nctarheel06
<Content>Friendly staff and convenient location, but cleanliness is questionable We stayed at the Aqua Aloha Surf for 3 nights 4/28-5/30. The lobby is very welcoming and so was the front desk attendant. Providing two bottled waters was a nice treat. As people had forewarned, the parking garage was tiny and when we arrived, there were two spaces that had been reserved by phone, but unclaimed. He told me to check back in 30 minutes and if they were still unclaimed, he would give me a permit. He was nice enough to call the room 15 minutes later and inform me that I could have one of the spaces. If we didn't have a reserved space, I could see that parking would be very inconvenient and feel a little unsafe since the external parking is dark.The room itself is indeed tiny. We had reserved superior city view through expedia so it wasn't the smallest room, but I'd still say that it was definitely smaller than most hotel rooms that I've stayed in. The bathroom clearly needed renovations as it seemed like an old residential bathroom. It needed caulking and had rusty drain fixtures. I'd equate it to a dorm bathroom. It was also very cramped - there was a sliding bathroom door separating the toilet from the sink and the toilet paper was attached to the door. There was also a small closet that was separated by a curtain rather than a door. You could clearly hear outdoor noise alhough my husband is a sound sleeper and it didn't bother him. The walls are thin, however. When we were there, they had people from the junior USTA tennis league staying there and we heard them talking and laughing pretty late into the night. The only other complaint I have is that when I woke up to get a drink from the mini fridge, I saw a roach crawling along the wall directly adjacent to my son's pack n play. That was not comforting since I wondered the rest of the time if it would crawl into his bed or our suitcases. I also didn't feel comfortable walking on the carpet without shoes on.All-in-all, I'd say it was an okay place to stay, minus the roach. I'm surprised that it is ranked as #21 in popularity though by others(I'd rank it much lower and would consider it 2 stars). Here's a summary of the pros and cons.Positives: Staff are nice, free continental breakfast (though we ended up going to Keoni's after the first day as another reviewer had recommended -- EXCELLENT place for breakfast and much more satisfying!!), reasonable price, mini fridge and microwave are nice to have, very convenient to full grocery store and restaurants and shops, friendly front desk staff, free internet (they even loaned us a new cable at no charge when we forgot ours)Negatives: Not convenient walk to the beach when you have a child and are carrying things with you, bathroom needs updating, cramped quarters, bugs/cleanlinessAlso a note - while the front desk staff are nice, don't bother asking for advice from the Expedia Local Expert in the lobby. I purchased a Honolulu Power Pass from Expedia and thought it would be convenient to run some questions and gain insight from the Expedia local expert. Boy was I wrong, she was unfriendly and I'd say rude. I presented her with the list of activities included on the pass and she wasn't familiar with half of them and pretty much said she coudldn't help me because she didn't know what I was interested in. It was a complete waste of time and left me with a bad taste in my mouth. I went back to her a second time to ask another question and she was again, useless. Don't expect a friendly person who knows much about what to see and do in the area.

<Content>Above and Beyond The Call Of Duty We had 4 nights at the Aloha Surf and had been impressed with the standard of accommodation and level of customer service BUT it was on the last night that we were completely blown away and humbled by a wonderful example of 'human spirit' and kindness from the front desk staff that night. We had returned from a day tour to the north shore. We explained what had happend to us which was why we needed to book the cheapest shuttle possible.While we were waiting one of the staff took me aside and put some money into my hand. The staff had given us money from their own pocket to help us out. The fact that these people were prepared to help out complete strangers, really restored our faith in the human spirit. We thank them very much and we fully recommend a stay at the Aloha Surf.

<Author>highlandbride
<Content>OK budget hotel if you are willing to put up with inconveniences First room on 9th floor was a horror, with one twin and one double (shoved up against the wall with totally worn out mattress) not the queen room we reserved. We paid an additional $40 a night (a good ploy they use to generate income) for a room on top floor with King bed, plus tub/shower combo. Regardless of floor position the noise is constant, especially late at night as bar patrons head out between 1AM - 4AM and the garbage trucks pick up the empty bottles at 5AM. Window AC and louvered windows do not keep room very cool and the noise from AC is not enough to block out the din on the streets. Curtains are cheap motel style black outs without any sheers so you must keep them closed when moving between closet and shower area (unless you don't care about exposing yourself to hundreds of adjacent neighbors in apartment buildings and hotels that surround the place). On the plus side the desk staff went out of their way to be helpful and Josh at the spa gives a killer shiatsu massage. Free breakfast is a starch-fest with pastries, bagels and bananas with juice and coffee. Go to Keoki's down the street for their $3.95 special - 2 pancakes, 2 bacon strips, scrambled eggs and coffee. The stroll to the beach was 2 long blocks and quick - the least objectionable of the soft mattresses, crummy curtains and scraped/worn furnishings that are showing age quickly after the refurbishment.

<Author>Dalaguete
<Content>An overall good hotel in Waikiki! We were here at the Aqua Aloha from March 10 - 14, and did not encounter any real problems, (except for the overpriced parking, which is really unavoidable, and the sloooooow elevators).However...Loved the little kitchen, comfy beds, breezy lobby, and proximity to the Food Pantry supermarket (which also houses a Coffee Bean). Walking to the beach is easy, and sundry items like tatami mats, disposable cameras and snacks can be picked up at the multitude of ABC stores on every corner on the way.I was thinking that staying at a hotel that was not fronting the beach would be a problem and it wasn't at all. It's a short stroll and the weather is always mild (sometimes windy enough to blow your swimsuit coverup over your head!). Also glad to get a renovated room, which was on the 6th floor. Obtained our travel package via bookit.com, which automatically gave us a deluxe (renovated) room. The view was of other ho-hum highrises, and I'm sure a view of the Ala Wai canal would have been much better.I would absolutely stay here again!

<Author>flippy2
<Content>A fine hotel for the price We stayed at the Aqua Aloha from Feb 11-26th, 2008. We had a queen bed with a pullout couch and a lanai on the 6th floor. We were travelling with a four month old infant and brought our own play yard, as the hotel was going to charge $20 per night for the use of a crib. Overall our experience there was fine--the location is good for Waikiki, as are the prices as compared to other hotels. I agree with another reviewer's opinion that the walk from Perrys Smorgy to the hotel is very dark at night, and made me uneasy when I had to walk to the hotel one night alone. During the day is no problem. The ABC store and Pantry grocery store are very close, which is great. There are also apples on the front desk throughout the day for eating. The continental breakfast was somewhat disappointing, but toward the end of our stay they added toasters with toast, bagels, cream cheese, and so on, in addition to the muffin, pastry, and mini croissant choices. Perhaps they are listening to people on this forum?!?! There is also juice, and coffee. My husband was not impressed by the breakfast, as he travels often and is used to the more hearty fare provided by Hampton/Hilton brands; however, I thought it was ok, especially as most hotels in Hawaii do not offer this service at all. We found housekeeping was alright, but we found our vanity countertop small and was not wiped down once during our 14 day stay. We thought it was because we had our toiletry bags on the counter, but we removed them two days in a row, and still the sink area was not cleaned. In all fairness to the hotel, though, we did not complain and simply wiped it up ourselves. We only had a shower stall in our room. The internet was free and fast (we brought our own laptop)--a great amenity for us. In general, we thought the hotel was average--an old hotel that has been updated, like most hotels in Waikiki. For the price, I would stay there again and would not worry about recommending this hotel to my friends.

<Author>Eirene22
<Content>Very pleased with the Aqua Aloha Surf We stayed at the Aloha Surf Hotel for 10 days in January and were very pleased with our choice. I had read on Expedia that the rooms were small, so we reserved a Superior Room. Though still a little small, we were pleased to have a corner room on the twelfth floor. We had a king-size bed, and wrap-around windows, plus the huge patio door onto the lanai. We could look over the Koolau Mountains, the Ala Wai Canal, and even see the ships on the ocean, as well as glimpses of Diamond Head between the hotels in the distance. The staff was wonderfully friendly, and very helpful. There were many complementary perks: delicious continental breakfast - muffins, buns, tropical fruit juice, coffee and four varieties of fresh fruit every morning; free daily paper; free in-room safe; free coffee for the in-room coffee maker; free Wireless in the lobby and pool area, and free high-speed connection in the room. They supplied the connector cable and when we had trouble, got it resolved very quickly by putting us in touch with their Net provider. They gave us each a bottle of chilled spring water when we checked in, and there was always a basket of delicious apples available on the lobby desk. We were given an Aqua coupon book, which we used extensively, both for restaurants and sightseeing. The coupons for the zoo, aquarium, Bishop's Museum, Mission Houses Museum, etc. were all two for one. The pool, though not large, was inviting, as was the sunny deck around it. We enjoyed eating our breakfast in the canopied open area beside the pool or on our lanai, enjoying the view. There were a lot of sirens in the evening, being so close to the hustle and bustle of Waikiki, but the garbage pickup shortly after 6 AM only woke us briefly. We felt very fortunate to only have to cross the parking lot to reach Perry's Smorgy or The Food Pantry ( our favourite restaurant and grocery store.) The walk to the beach was only a few blocks, passing the quaint King's Village Shopping mall on the way. This was our second trip to Hawaii. We would definitely go back to the Aloha Surf. It is not new or flashy, but the location, the staff, the cleanliness and the value for money, make us recommend it.  
<Date>Feb 19, 2008

<Author>tripchick29
<Content>Great hotel--better price! I stayed at this hotel Christmas week in December 2007. It is one of the smaller hotels in Waikiki, which when you see the size of some of them, is a very good thing.The first room I stayed in was very, very noisy (as other reviews here also state). Not only did the garbage truck come by the first morning, but it turns out that the side of this building is a parking lot/loading zone to a grocery store on the next corner. This meant that large trucks were beginning their deliveries to this store from 6am onwards. As a note, this hotel does not have the normal type glass windows that I would expect to find in a highrise hotel here in Canada. The windows are thick fibreglass slats, opening and closing like venetian blinds, so the noise level was not muffled at all.After complaining at the front desk, I was shown a slightly smaller (but nicer) room on the 9th floor to the back and middle of the building. Once I moved there, the noise level was considerably lower and I enjoyed the rest of my stay fully.There isn't much of a view from this hotel at all. After moving from a larger corner suite to the quieter room, the only view available was to the neighbours' balconies. However, considering I spent little time in my room it was fine.The other negative to this hotel is that I found the bathrooms, especially bathtub/shower to be very old and outdated and slightly grungy. Do not expect to be able to take a relaxing bath in a luxurious hotel bathtub at this hotel.The pool is very small--enough to take a quick dip in, but it also backs into the very active, noisy grocery store parking lot.Apart from the above, my stay was great and I would definitely stay at this hotel again (booking a room at the back/middle portion of the hotel from the onset). The front desk staff were extremely helpful and friendly, elevators were fast, there was a small breakfast of fruit, fruit juice, coffee and small muffins each morning (enough to get your started). The housekeepers did an excellent job and the room was kept tidy and clean.There is a mini fridge, coffee maker, and microwave with dishes in the room as well which came in handy a couple of times.The location is excellent--two blocks away from Waikiki with food stores, Starbucks, whatever you want nearby.This hotel is undergoing renovations and I think when they are completed, it will definitley be 5/5 on Trip Advisor as a budget hotel. They had just opened a spa when I arrived (great specials on massages) and were in the process of adding a small coffee shop in the lobby.

<Author>sgalluc
<Content>Great location, good value for the money I was a little worried about staying at this hotel but was very surprised at how nice it was. The lobby is beautiful, open walkway, nice furniture, and a great place to eat breakfast. The pool is a little small but was never crowded and the lounge chairs were very comfortable. Breakfast consisted of rolls, muffins, fruit, coffee, and pineapple juice (yum!) Coffee, newspapers, apples, and internet were available around the clock. A vending machine with pop, water, and juice was available. Ask to stay in a deluxe room or suite and in the front of the hotel. The views from the back of the hotel are awful. We asked to switch rooms and they were able to that for us that day. There isn't a lot of parking available if you rent a car so ask ahead of time for a spot. The elevators are a little small and slow so plan extra time for that. The staff was very nice, and very helpful with planning transportation and tours. Although, the 2 tours we booked through the hotel were not worth the money. Book any tourist events through the company directly. The beach is only a few blocks away and there are plenty of great restaurants near buy as well as shopping and the famous ABC store. All in all, this a great value for the money. I recommend the location if you want to be in the heart of Waikiki, you don't mind little noise (especially in the morning), and you don't want to spend too much money.

<Author>coywan
<Content>Pleasant Surprise for the Price My wife and I love Hawaii and visit twice a year. We've stayed at various types of hotels and condos but the Aqua Aloha is probably the best value we've gotten for our money. When I pulled up to the hotel in my rental vehicle, I was in the valet driveway and was told I could leave it there while I check in. I went up to the front desk, gave my name, and I was handed my room keys and parking permit in less than a minute (like they had everything ready for me). Check-in process was the fastest I've experienced. Parking is limited but I never had a problem finding a spot the whole week I was there. When I got to the room, I realized that I was upgraded to the 16th floor corner room with a wrap around balcony. I had views of the Ala Wai Canal, the back side of Diamond Head, and a partial ocean view between the Hyatt Regency towers (where I stayed for my last visit in Waikiki). Room was very clean and had a refridgerator, microwave, and LCD TV. Staff was very nice all week except when I went down for continental breakfast with a paper plate. I was told they were not allowed and I had to use napkins to carry the pastries. But oh well, I still managed to bring 6 croissants to my room where I would heat up bacon and spam in the microwave oven. It was very convenient having a refrigerator and microwave. I never had to buy alcohol at a bar all week. At night, my wife and I would mix our drinks in the room, get wasted, then walk/shop. Every morning, we would go to the front desk for beach towels and turn them in when we return. If you vacation for the destination and not the room, then you get great value at the Aqua Aloha Surf.

<Author>timidtravelerUs
<Content>Of the people I can write 2 reviews of the Aqua Aloha, because we stayed in 2 very different rooms during our stay. But first, if friendly helpful people are important to you on your trips, then you are in for treat at Aqua Aloha Surf, as the staff was friendly, down to earth and helpful.We stayed here to save a little money on the last leg of our trip. The first rooms we stayed in were the basic rooms, and they reminded me of European hotels, small, very basic, but with comfortable beds. No lanai. The bathrooms sliding doors are flimsy and a little off-putting. A little worn down, but the room was clean. As the night wore on, I felt like I was camping in Waikiki, because the louver windows didn't close all the way so we left them open. The wind rustled , heard the palm trees and the traffic, it was cool. However, the traffic and trucks are very noisy in the morning. These rooms I would recommend if you want clean inexpensive lodging and don't plan on being in room at all. If traffic noise will bother you, don't stay in the basic rooms! You can't avoid it.The next night we got upgraded to the one bedroom suite. This had a nice lanai with ocean and mountain views. Nice king bed and less comfortable pull out sofa bed. Nice kitchenette with plates, microwave and 2 refrigs. Bathroom still small with flimsy door. Windows still didn't close completely so we left them open and didn't use ac at all. Traffic not so noticeable up here, although you hear it, and I loved hearing the birds roost in the neighboring banyan tree. This room I would recommend for family travel. It is not elegant, but it was pleasant and comfortable. The breakfast is pretty bad. We made coffee in our room, as the coffee downstairs is terrible! I would eat a banana and an apple and a little juice. Muffins and pastries were not good.  
<Date>Dec 30, 2007

<Author>SFBayAreaTraveller
<Content>Somewhere between average and above average If there is one thing I loved about this hotel, it was its location. It is conveniently located to almost all the places you want to go in Waikiki: the zoo, the beach, the parks, the shopping district and restaurants. This, for me, is very important. If you are a budget traveller and are enticed by other hotels that may offer a cheaper rate but is a good distance away from Waikiki's sweet spot as I call it, you will be making a big mistake that you will eventually regret. I have traveled to more than 40 countries on a shoe string budget and have learned from trial and error that it is worth paying a little more to be where you want to be. That being said, our deluxe room which was on the 6th floor was very basic. When we arrived, I was actually disappointed at the condition of the room. The walls, the bathroom, and the sofa were a bit old and faded. It reminded me of those old vegas hotels in old downtown Las Vegas. Moreover, and this might be a biggie for some people, if you are a light sleeper, than you should think twice about this hotel. There is a lot of noise coming from the surrounding area at night. I had no problem with the noise, but my wife apparently did and had difficulty sleeping. because of the sound of automobiles, trucks, and late party goers.But to be fair, there were amenities that the room contained the offsets the condition of the room such as a safe, microwave, coffee maker, mini fridge, mini sink, hair drier, A.C., free internet, and did I mention the superb location? The hotel staff were very helpful. They were always ready to answer any of our questions.

<Author>Xinger2
<Content>Good rate, good location, good service My wife and I traveled from Vancouver, Canada, for a vacation/anniversary celebration. Because of lengthy delays in flights due to snow (no wonder we were headed to Hawaii) we arrived at the Aloha Surf well after 1:00 am. very tired and on the verge of grumpiness. The front desk attendant was efficient and had us checked in with our room keys within a few short minutes. When we turned to get our luggage we saw them already stacked on the porter's trolley. We eventually got to bed at almost 2:00 a.m. (4:00 a.m. Vancouver time). The next morning we were disturbed by the sound of garbage trucks picking up the large bins at an early hour. From previous reviews I was aware of this situation that affects rooms on the street side of the hotel and was able to drift back to sleep. Garbage pickup took place the next morning also (Saturday) but we had adjusted somewhat to the time difference and going to bed at an earlier time. We found the bed to be too close to the air conditioner causing cold air to blow straight onto our faces but this was solved by turning around so as to sleep with our heads at the foot of the bed. Our Hawaiian island cruise was scheduled to depart at 8:00 p.m and Aloha Surf was able to store our luggage after check-out time until we collected our luggage at mid-afternoon. The day before the ship was scheduled to return to Honolulu we found out that the cruise line's arrangements for left luggage were unsuitable to meet our 10:20 p.m. flight departure. We telephoned Aloha Surf from Kaua'i island and explained that we were guests a week earlier and had a problem finding a place to store only luggage from morning to night. The very quick answer from person who answered the Aloha Surf phone was that it was no problem. Eventually we were given a peek of the storage room and it was packed with luggage. The receptionist said that it is a service that they normally offer. This was a really a tremendous help to us, allowing us to enjoy Honolulu for the whole day. This, in addition to the excellent location and bargain price ($76), made our stay with Aloha Surf a great experience.

<Author>LiveAlohaForever
<Content>hidden charges, internet down, no parking I'm a frequent visitor to Hawaii (5 times this year, and 2-3 trips each year for the past 29 years) who has several favorite hotels, but I wanted to try something different. I picked Aqua Aloha Surf based on TripAdvisor reviews, its free internet service (I had to work during this trip), and its theme--I love to surf; so the theme and lobby pics were appealing, and the location's only a 5-minute walk to Queen's and Canoe's, where it's fun to paddle out, or even just hang out and listen to surf legends like Rabbit Kekai swap stories while they watch the surf. I also like the local's bar directly across the street from the hotel, because it has decent, surprisingly cheap food and drinks and it serves late-night dinners. Just be aware that this bar's a local's hangout, and the locals can get a bit boisterous, even those who are serving you! (Show some respect...kinda like being in the line-up at Makaha's, if you dare!)Unfortunately, I was sorely disappointed by the hotel, mostly because of unexpected charges on my AmX bill, by the lack of internet service in my room the first two days--which were days I was supposed to be working--and by the extreme coldness of one female manager and one male desk clerk (the rest of the staff were great--total aloha). The charges I didn't expect were a $48.00 service fee from reservetravel.com and $64.00 car deposit fee. I tried calling the hotel about these charges, but was unsuccessful, so I ended up disputing the charges by writing AmX. AmX eventually reported that the hotel refused to cancel either charge. Apparently, the service fee was the result of some ridiculously vague fine print that I didn't read (who does) when booking the reservation...it said there MAY be a service fee of $0 to $5 per room/per night. The charge for the car was equally bad...I had the car for only a SINGLE night, as I told the desk clerk when I picked up the parking pass. The hotel's lot was full, so I had to park in a really grimy lot at the Continental several blocks away. I kind of expected this parking situation based on other TripAdvisor reports. But what I really didn't expect was a $64.00 charge for ONE night of parking! Because of these charges, no Aqua hotels will ever get my business again.

<Author>shelbymom
<Content>In the thick of it...Bring ear plugs! We liked the location better than the Aqua Palms which we had stayed at last year. The Aloha is just a couple of blocks from all shops/restaurants/people. I suppose if you have children and plan to spend a lot of time at the beach this location wouldn't work that well. Strolling to the beach was easy, but if we had to lug towels, mats, snacks, drinks, toys, etc., we may have found it a bit of a hassle. Finding a parking space in Honolulu isn't always an easy task either.The open air lobby was attractive and the desk clerk (Jason, I think) and the porter (Jeremy?) couldn't have been nicer. Our room, number 503, was on a corner near a store parking lot with views into neighboring apartment buildings. I have never heard so many beep, beep, beeps from trucks backing up in my life! There was A LOT of noise, so either bring earplugs, ask for a higher room, or try a different side of the building. No big deal - Part of life in the big city. That parking lot I mentioned provides quick access to the marketnext store which also has a Coffee Bean and Tea Leaf, donut shop, and another little pastry place inside. Handy since we never managed to get downstairs to the continental breakfast in time. I thought our room was better looking than it appeared on the internet. The colors, soft greens and blues, looked washed out on the computer screen but more vibrant in person. Nice to have a little sofa, coffee table, microwave, frig, and coffee maker in the room. Seems like they did a lot of renovating, but left the old tub and tile. Even though we tipped the maid every day her care of our room was somtimes sloppy. One day she gave us clean towels, no wash clothes, and didn't make thebed. Other little things seemed to be neglected, but nothing to botherthe management about. Pool area is attractive, though small. You can check-out beach towels from the front desk folks, which is nice. Afterreading other reviews on this site I'll add that our water pressure was great, we didn't see any seedy characters in the neighborhood, and it's just a pleasant hotel without pretentions.

<Author>haleiwa311
<Content>Best Hotel Value In Hawaii Although this hotel hardly needs another 5 star rating, it was such a surprise and great experience I will try to give a different perspective.I was a Vice President for one the largest hotel chains in the world and have stayed in many hotels throughout the world over 30 years. I also have a second home in Hawaii and have been going to Hawaii since 1968. The first comment that comes to mind is that Aqua Resorts have really got their act together. I have not seen a such a combination of value, decor, friendliness, amenities and service.This hotel use dynamic sales, much like airlines, so your rate will vary depending on demand but it will remain the best value in Waikiki since demand is essentially seasonal and will affect other hotels as well.My first impression was the striking decor of the lobby and four employees at the front desk in about a 150 room hotel--you would be lucky to have that many in a 1000+ room hotel.Then to my room which was tastefully decorated as I've seen in a long time. Many of the few negative reviews complain of small rooms. I found the size well designed and more than adequate. The amenities were first class and the refrigerator, microwave and coffee are rare to find in hotels costing three times the price. The bathrobes were unique and the most luxurious I've seen anywhere--not the usual terry short white robe if they are provided at all. Also unique was having live anthuriums. The lanai was large and a view of the Ali Wai canal and the green mountains of the Monoa valley. . The beach is only a few blocks away and it is a bit quieter at this hotel location and has the only super market in Waikiki next door. The only thing I would add to the room would be a night light and small reading chair--but you can use the lanai chairs.The desk staff was always extremely friendly and the engineers , Craig and Mark, were very helpful in setting up my own dvd player and replacing a defective phone. Again for the few negative reviewers it's to be expected that sometimes things go wrong but what is important is that it is corrected. Try to get this kind of service in 2000 room hotel! It' s obvious that the employees enjoy their jobs are truly examples of the Aloha Spirit.Two other extras are the free broadband connection(hotels on the beach charge up to $20/day) and the free continental breakfast.The bottom line is that you will not find a better value in Waikiki, maybe not anywhere. Of course, if you must be on the beach prepare to pay 3-4 times the price with 1/2 the experience. I am telling all my friends and neighbors in Hawaii about this hotel and since it is relatively new, most do not know about it. My friends and I rarely go to Waikiki but it is much improved over 10 years ago and I would definitely pick this hotel again.David C. Johnson

<Author>Lori1558
<Content>Honolulu Value We began out island hopping vacation at the Aqua Aloha Surf. Check in with Vinh was great. He is quiet but nice and professional. After living in Hawaii for a number of years, I learned that the local people are really sensitive to tone. So, if you need something changed, be sweet.Our deluxe room was wonderful and clean. Located on the 14th floor away from the streetside on the front of the hotel, we had a view of the Alai Wai Canal, golf course and mountains. It was not plush; however, for as much time we spent in the room, it was perfect with fridge, sink and microwave. The breakfast was minimal and be prepared for an $18 per day parking fee if you have a rental car. Access from hotel to H1 was easy going by the canal to McCully and straight on to H1. Would stay here again. Don't miss their free happy hour on Tuesday evening. Great specialty drink!

<Author>SharonKai
<Content>Great place to stay My husband and I travelled from Australia and stayed here for 8 nights in October 2007. We booked a Superior room and were very happy with it. As expected, it was a little noisy (traffic) during the day but at night it quietened down. Our flight into Honolulu arrived early in the morning and check in to the hotel wasn't until 3.00pm. We got to the hotel by 11.00am and they stored our bags until 3.00pm. There is plenty of seating in the foyer and also free coffee or tea for guests. The front desk also has complimentary fruit for guests. We were on the 5th floor (room 510) and the room was on a corner of the building. We had beautiful views looking over the canal and up the mountain - just gorgeous at night. I know other people have said that the rooms are small but we found ours more than adequate. The breakfast, which was included in the tariff, was adequate for us - pastries, juice  fruit. Our room was always kept very clean and we found the cleaning staff very friendly. Most of the front office staff were friendly and helpful BUT a couple were also not so friendly or helpful!! Two people we found on the front desk who were great were Helene and Jennifer. They were always helpful and very friendly. The location is great - close to buses, restaurants, shops and only a couple of blocks from Waikiki Beach. We found the Food Pantry store next door great for supplies. The Honolulu bus system (The Bus) is great - $2 is all you will pay to go anywhere (even Hanaume Bay) - don't forget to ask the driver for a return ticket when you get on. If you get back on a bus within a couple of hours it's free! If you need a change from breakfast at the hotel, there are many restaurants close by - even a Denny's if you want a cheap meal. Parking is a problem at the hotel. If you are lucky enough to get a park it will cost you $15 per night. If you do get a park, ensure you get a permission to park notice from the front office staff to display in your car, otherwise you may get towed away! The parking lot of the Food Pantry next door is also available at night but from memory you could only park between 6.00pm until 7.00am. Each room has a safe in it and this was free. There is a laundry in the basement to do your washing and each room also has an iron and ironing board. Don't pack a beach towel as you can get these from the front desk when you need them. We had a great Thai meal at the Ohana East Hotel nearby and great pizza at a restaurant in the International Marketplace. Do the walk up Diamond Head but go early in the morning - the views are wonderful. Cost us $4 each on the bus (return) and $1 entry  take a bottle of water. I would recommend this hotel and would stay there again.  
<Date>Oct 21, 2007

<Author>picturejoy
<Content>good price, clean room, but painful parking My friend and I stayed at this hotel for 5 nights, we booked deluxe room with two beds. The first room we got, has a bed and a sofa, so I went down to front desk, Vinh did change a room for me, but not in a friendly way, he said that the sofa can be pulled out as a bed, so, it is indeed a two beds room. (BTW, all the times we were there, I have to deal with Vinh in several cases, he never smiles). Anyway, our new room has 2 beds, and a sofa, it is clean, has more than we need, and I am glad that there is a safety box in the closet. As everyone said, it only has shower, but that is not a problem for us. The free breakfast is not fancy, but we are not 'big breakfast' person at all, so, juice/banana/muffin is good enough to start a day. Also, the hotel provides beach tower to guests(just ask the front desk for it). Parking is a nightmare, we were glad that we insisted on having a compact car when we picked up our car at rental (they wanted to give us a minivan and other big cars). The space are very small and limited, you have to be extremely careful.Overall, this hotel is in a great location, blocks away from all the Waikiki activities, and a grocery store right by it, price is cheap, room is clean, and has everything you need. If you are on budget, definitely check this one out.

<Author>Jetblast25
<Content>Great Value and All Around Excellent I was there post-cruise earlier this month (Sept). Pre-cruise, we stayed at the Hyatt Waikiki, which was very disappointing. When I compare the 2 hotels, and their amenities, I have to say- don't waste your money at the Hyatt. Online, the Aloha Surf is about 1/3 the price. The Aloha is 2 blocks from the beach, 1 block from The Bus and has great rooms, amenities and staff. Like I said, I was at the Hyatt earlier, and was disgusted that in spite of a $300/nt room, they wanted to charge me $19/day for a fridge in my room (i had to notify them to opt out), and other nickel and dime fees. This place has free refridgerator, microwave, bathrobes, flat screen, beach towels, in-room i'net, free cont'l breakfast and even a comp manager's cocktail party on Tues. The rooms are bright and cheerful, the staff are great people and while the pool is small, the chairs are soooo comfortable. Also, there's a great ABC shop just across the street with a bigger selection than the ABC in the Hyatt. I know you'll think the Hyatt must be better if it costs so much more, but really, it's completely overpriced and neither the location (across the street from the beach), nor the service warrant such a price.Book the Aloha Surf, you won't be disappointed.

<Author>Hove-UK-Traveller
<Content>Very good value. Parking a pain! We stayed in the Aqua Aloha Surf for 4 nights from August 16th. It is a really good value hotel in a good location. On arrival we left the car in the hotel car park only to be told by staff we would need to move it, as it was full. I let the member of staff on reception know how annoyed I was that the car park was full and that the price was now $18 a night (I'd emailed the hotel 2 months before to enquire about the price, they told me it would be $13/night - a large price increase). To their credit they offered us an upgrade to my room, which made us feel happier! They allow you to use the car park in another Aqua hotel, which was about 4 blocks away. I read that it is their intention to turn this service into a valet system. That would be a very good idea. I think until this service is available they need to make it clear on their website that parking is limited.After recovering from the car park trauma we went to the room, which was lovely, recently modernised, and with a kitchenette (since we'd been upgraded). There was a locked adjoining door to the room next door from which we could hear the guest next to us coughing. Not too bad, but noisier people would have been very easy to hear.There is a free breakfast of muffins  fruit, which was a nice extra.The hotel is a few minutes walk from Waikiki beach and all the local shops.Staff were courteous but not over-friendly.All in all, excluding the parking situation, the hotel provides very good value for money (we paid $99/night) in terms of the room condition and location.

<Author>nextcube
<Content>A bargain near the beach We took a gamble when we booked the Aloha Surf. We'd had reservations for the Hilton Hawaiian Village for the week of a conference, but after some discussion, we decided that we wanted to spend more on our exhibit for the conference and less on accomodations. In the end, we're glad we did.The Aloha Surf's building is an older one; from the looks of it, early 1960's. It's been extensively remodeled since.The rooms are small, but tidy and have attractive furniture. Room amenities are good - bathrobe, iron and ironing board, fridge and coffee maker. LCD TVs are a nice touch. Small key-operated safe in the closet; you get the keys from the front desk at check-in. Complimentary wired high-speed internet service in the rooms works well. This is an older building, so you get a window air conditioner as opposed to a built-in climate control system. My room (a deluxe room) had a balcony with a couple of chairs, and a sofa and coffee table. One of my co-workers had a standard room which didn't get the sofa or coffee table.The lobby area is smaller than it looks in the photos (and the chairs there aren't particularly comfortable) but it's airy and inviting. It's also outside, which you can't tell from the pictures, meaning it gets pretty warm and wet there while you're waiting to check in.The guest laundry could probably use another washer/dryer or two, since it seemed there was always a line down there.Parking is also cramped; they only have 18 parking spaces (and charge $18/day) so keep that in mind if you're renting a car (it was a non-issue for me - I bought a bus pass!)In the end, it was a good hotel. For where it is and what we paid, it was an excellent deal.

<Author>SavvyDesigner
<Content>Looks can be deceiving I had researched this hotel plus many competitors before booking this trip. Its website raves it as a newly renovated boutique hotel. Their whole branding/marketing was also quite stylish. My BF and I booked a standard queen room, but had no idea it was going to be so small. Although it does seem to have new wallcovering/carpets, and furniture, there was really nothing they can do with the space limitation. The bathrooms were small, pedestal sink with no counter space, a very tight shower stall (with a faulty shower head that we had to ask to be replaced), and a sliding barn door into the bathroom because there was not enough space for a real door. The air conditioner was the worst, it was on the window wall and positioned right at bed level, the bed was literally less than 3 feet from the unit, so if you slept at night, you had a constant rush of cold air shooting directly at your face. Not to mention it was loud. We had to strategically move the guest chair in front of the unit and then clothes, bags, and anything on the chair to prevent the air from heating us. We would shut off the air, except the room gets very stuffy and also windows have no screens so we would be mosquito dinner if we had left the windows open. The staff was friendly, very helpful, when we had our rooms cleaned it seems like they never replaced our bedsheets or pillow cases, they just fixed it up, not a great cleaning effort. Parking was also a rip-off, $15/day. So we only had a car for 2 days out of the 6 days we were there. Everything is walkable or can be accessible by bus, but you will want to have a car to drive to some other very beautiful places, otherwise you are really missing the true beauty of Oahu. The only plus was the hotel was at a great convenient location. Close to public transportation and stores/restaurants. Somewhat quiet street.

<Author>rwalker66
<Content>Adequate if all you need is a place to sleep About as far from Waikiki Beach that you can be without being in the Ala Wai Canal. You have to cross both busy Kuhio Avenue and Kalakaua Avenue to reach the beach. And when you walk down the street the hotel is on at night it is quite dark due to overhanging trees and inadequete lighting. There were also some iffy characters hanging out in that darkened section including 2 people who looked like they were about to come to blows.I was assigned a room on the 3rd floor. It had no balcony and no view - unless you count looking in other peoples windows a view. The windows in the room are the kind that are glass slats that you open and close by turning the handles. There are no screens to keep out the mosquitoes. Unfortunately when I entered my room one window was wide open and there was no way to close it as the handle was missing. My room was probably mosquito central by then. On my way out I informed the desk staff and it had been fixed when I returned an hour later.I had to have the window A/C unit on 24/7 it was so hot. The air conditioner would make a very loud noise every 15 minutes on schedule which can make getting to sleep difficult. I brought a white noise machine from home and put it on the loud setting right next to my ear, that helped some. The shower was the size of a phone booth so if you are a person of size you might get stuck in there. Also if you are over 5'8 good luck getting a shampoo. I'm 6'2 and the shower head was about 6 inches lower than my head. I had to sort of squat and bend over sideways to get my head wet. Also both faucets were labelled C for cold, so good luck your first time in figuring out which one is which. You might get scalded.There was a sign in the elevator saying the pool was closed from October 11 until a date to be determined. I don't use pools but just an FYI in case you wanted to. It said you could use the pool at another Aqua hotel if that helps. Have fun finding it.Breakfast has gone downhill since the previous reviews. It was not delivered to my door, and there was no can of iced tea or nice yogurt. You went down to the lobby and got a piece of fruit out of a basket or muffins out of other baskets. For drinks they had those big clear plastic dispensers where you can dispense a cup of orange juice or pineapple juice. There was a coffee machine too although it said you had to pay $2.00 for some of the coffees.Some of the staff were rude and when you went to the front desk they would ignore you for a while then look up like Why are you bugging me?. There was a real nice young Asian girl there though who was friendly and attentive. She was the exception rather than the rule.There is free wireless broadband but I don't have a laptop so that was no good to me. They should have some desktops set up to use for free.Pluses:Grocery store close by, modern furnishings, LCD TV with about 30 channels including MTV and VH1 (although I only watched the TV when eating breakfast in my room or at night when I got in), free internet access if you have a laptop. Fridge, microwave, coffee maker and hair dryer in room, hangers you can actually remove from the closet, price to stay there, close to International Marketplace, free daily newspapers, and a free safe in the room. So basically if all you need is a place to sleep, don't need a pool, don't mind a long walk to the beach, and don't mind some room problems then this place should be adequate for you.

<Author>gsnichol
<Content>Decent place for the price This hotel was one of the better value that I found when I was searching. Sure, it's not on Waikiki beach but it's only about a 10-15 minute walk away. The rooms are quite small; I think two people would have been almost on top of one another in the room I had. The room was airconditioned and I used this most of the time since although Honolulu is quite breezy which tempers the humidity, the position of the window wasn't always where the wind was blowing.The hotel offers breakfast which is little more than a can of orange juice and a cake, but you can drink and nibble as you get dressed. The hotel also had wired internet which was reliable.I did see one or two street girls in that area but that is pretty typical for Waikiki so if you ignore that then the hotel is good value for money. Be prepared to pay for the car parking space, and you have to reserve it in advance.

<Author>chris1916
<Content>Aqua Aloha Surf Rocks We booked this hotel through Delta as a combined Air/Hotel package for a week. I would definately come back and stay here. They upgraded us when we arrived and were given a room on the top floor that had a view of the Ala Wai Canal and Waikiki. If noise bothers you, then I would suggest getting a hotel outside of Waikiki. Waikiki is the hub of this island and everyone stays here. Continental breakfast delivered to the room each morning when requested. Nice touch! The front desk staff were always friendly and greeted us with Aloha. My son said the sofa bed was on the uncomfortable side, but he was ok with it. There is an ABC (7-11) Store a block away for knick knacks and snacks. Also a smorgasboard restraunt on the same block that has a $10.95 dinner deal. Best food deal in the area. Buy your chocolate macadamian nut candy at the ABC store. If you wait until the airport, you will pay triple the price. The hotel does not have a big parking garage. We paid $50 for a week of parking at the Waikiki Banyan about 4 blocks away. I enjoyed the walk to pick up the car when needed. This is a great hotel with a great staff. We will stay here again.
