<Author>SRiches
<Content>Bit noisy and rubbish shower, but otherwise ok We stayed here for 2 nights - October 11 and 12 and paid around $95 for a queen bed in a superior room.To summarise : if you're prepared to accept the downsides below, I think it's a good place to stay in Waikiki bearing in mind there are limited options in the 'under $100' price range ! NoiseThe design of the windows meant that they didn't close properly so, despite being on the 14th floor, we heard a bit of street noise from around 6am - the noisy refuse collection (as another reviewer mentioned) and cars on the street. However, I think some noise is to be expected in a city so we didn't mind too much. In addition, the air con unit was pretty noisy. Ear plugs would be a good idea :-) Rubbish showerThe shower was clean and well - kept but the water came out as little more than a dribble and it was the worst waterflow of the 7 hotels / condos during our trip round California and Oahu! WorksThere were notices in the lobby saying :1) from October 'until further notice' the pool is closed (I think it said for safety reasons) - this didn't bother us but I expect that some people would mind.2) they are doing work to several balconies so don't leave anything on your balcony etc - fortunately our balcony was not affected.3) they are doing work to the car park, which meant that there were only 8 or 9 underground spaces available - however, we got lucky and had a space on both days. They did give us a list of other places to park nearby, although I think they were open air so possibly less secure. BreakfastAs others have said, it was inadequate (a small muffin, can of iced tea, nice yoghurt) and was less than any other hotel breakfast on our trip in the same price bracket. On the plus side, it was delivered to your room and you could choose one of 4 20 minute time-slots, starting at 7.30am. Top tip: one day we went to the Seaside Cafe on Kuhio Avenue (8 mins walk) for a v. tasty $2.99 breakfast of pancakes, scrambled egg and bacon. Good points about the Aqua Aloha : nice location (our room overlooked the canal and golf course to the side), decent price, clean, the room was tastefully and recently decorated and in great condition. The flat screen TV was a nice touch too. The reception area had some comfy, colourful sofa's. Finally, if you can, pay a bit extra for a 'superior' room - after we'd opened our suitcases there was little room for manoevre so I dread to think how small the 'standard' rooms are :-)

<Content>Great Hotel for the following reasons: 1) Price 2) Microwave + refrigerator in every room 3) Knowledgable staff members and 4) Upon my return home, I realized I had forgotten some of my belongings in the hotel room - I quickly called the hotel and they sent me all my items! <Author>adaj
<Content>Hotel is nice but service sucks.... So I just got back on Wednesday from a wonderful 5 day 4 night stay in Waikiki. I have been to Hawaii many times before. I used to be a flight attendant, and not only did I have layovers in HNL, but I also took several vacations there. I am making it a point to write this review because trip advisor is how I ultimately decided to stay at the Aloha Surf hotel and hopefully this helps other vacationers out there. I started planning this trip about a month and a half ago. Once I decided to go back to Hawaii, I booked my vacation package on United Airlines. Through their website, there were many hotel options. I knew that I did not want to spend a lot of money on the hotel, because I wanted to be able to use that money on excursions and good eating. My brother just went to Hawaii for his one year anniversary and spent over $1400 to stay at the Hilton Hawaiin Village. Considering all he did was sleep there, I wasn't gonig to make the same mistake. I decided to stay at the Aloha Surf because it received pretty good reviews, was right in heart of Waikiki, and was definitely financially appealing.The pictures on tripadvisor are pretty accurate. I arrived at the hotel on Sat. morning and was impressed with the lobby. The lounge chairs, flat panel TV and blue lighting were nice and inviting. I was pretty happy with my decision. Usually hotel photos are much nicer than the real thing. In this case, I was impressed (at least for now). I walked up to the front desk where three guys were talking to eachother. One guy (I am guessing he is the Manager on Duty-sits at the desk on the side) told the other guy to check me in. They seemed bothered as if I was interrupting them. The check in was quick. Here are your keys. Enjoy your stay. I had to ask HIM how his day was going. No welcome, no can I help you with bags, nothing. I didn't event get a cold face towel at check in (I thought that was part of the deal) This was just the beginning of the service I would be receiving. The hotel room was nice, with new decor, comfortable beds, and an air conditioner that worked. The flat panel TV was nice, although limited channels, no pay per view or gaming options. And no automated voicemail system. My friend who lives there called the hotel several times. On time, he said the phone kept ringing and ringing, only to be later asnwered by someone at the Front Desk who rudely told him we were not in. Another time he called, housekeeping answered the phone. Not sure if that is protocal. Actually I know it is not. I am no longer a flight attendant, I now work as a Sales Manager for a large hotel chain. That is probably why I am noticing all these points.The next 4 days would be more routine, since I was now used to the hotel. I have to admit, location wise, the hotel is great. Just two blocks from the main street and Waikiki beack. The bus system is great and can take you just about anywhere for a couple bucks. The hotel itself was nice. Here are some pros and cons:Pros:Location-near everythingPrice-can't beat itNice rooms-decor and air conditiningCons:Service, Service, Service - On Sunday, we decided to go parasailing. I went downstairs and pulled a brochure for Hawaii Parasail from the brochure stand. Again, the gentleman who I am assuming is the Manager on Duty sitting at the desk to the side, looked at me like I was in his space. I asked him if Hawaii Parasail was a good company to go with and he replied rudely I wouldn't even know. You are a manager? Sitting at what one might confuse as a concierge desk? Live in Hawaii? Cater to tourists and vacationers? Must have parasailed at least one? And that is the best response I can get. Then later on he was at the desk when I asked for towels and made this face again like I was interupting him. I can tell you this. If he was working at my hotel, he would defnitely not be in a customer service position with us. Maybe dishwasher or laundry man. He needs to go!The front desk clerks just kept talking to eachother, joking around, and looking at guests as if we were at their door trying to sell them girl scout cookies or newspapers. That get off my porch before I shoot you look. NICE!No automated voicemail system and basic TV.Swimming pool is small and closed at 7pm. That's right. A swimming pool in Hawaii closed at 7pm. And one more point for the icing on the cake:I came back to the room on Monday around 2pm and housekeeping had not cleaned the room. That morning I noticed that the sheets had some blood stains. They were obviously clean sheets with older stains. No worries. I am in hospitality and understand. She came in to clean the room while I was in there, so I sat on the couch and watched TV. She went to straighten up the bed. Yes, straighten. Not change the sheets. Not change the pillow case. Straighten and re-tuck the sheets. I was in shock. I had to get up and show her the stain and asked her to change the whole bedding, which she did. I hate to think I was sleeping on the same sheets for 3 days but who knows.Well, originally I was going to say this hotel was well worth the money. For the budget minded it is definitely worth it. For someone who needs SOME decent customer service and hopefully clean sheets, this may not be the best hotel. Would I return. Maybe. If I do, I will definitely be more attentative to housekeeping and go with the knowledge that I won't get a whole lot out of the front desk. Why should I expect to? It's not like it's a SERVICE related job. Oh wait. IT IS! Never mind. I won't go back to Aloha Surf. I will go back to Aqua hotels though. I think they have a nice product, they just need to fine tune the service details. Maybe the other hotels are better. I will wait to see next year when I return. Until then, Mahalo!p.s. Not all the desk clerks were rude. On Tuesday morning when I checked out, I finally got the service I was hoping for. Thank you for staying with us and come back soon from a nice lady (pregnant) at the front desk. FINALLY! Didn't realize this wasn't going to be this long. Hope it helps.

<Author>MikekNZ
<Content>Worth the cost. I gave this 5/5  Why? Because it was worth the amount paid. It is not 5 star but then neither is the price.I stayed the previous 10 days at the Hilton Hawaiian Village at about 6x the cost and the HHV was not 6x better although still very good. The price paid was $80 per night booked via expedia. Includes internet and breakfast (the reasons i booked this place)The hotel was perfect for me, a single traveller finishing out the last couple of days in Hawaii in a different scene.  The room was small basically about 4x4m with a corner taken up by the bathroom - it was small but adequate. The fittings were the same as the pictures and more than adequate ( flat screen tv with 30 channels, microwave, coffee maker) The bathroom was average but not at all bad so overall the room is just fine if you plan to do what you should and spend most of the time exploring. Bed was fine and i had no problems sleeping. Pros:Clean room with the things you would expect TV is good and lots of channels to watch in the times in the room Free internet - cable in the room and wireless in the lobby - very easy to use and fast - with no seeming restrictions perfect for skype home etc Airconditioning - self controlled Free breakfast and paper (nothing special but free) Location - close to the action of the city and buses, resturants, abc stores etc. Lobby is nice and setup well for waiting for pickups etc.Cons: Older style windows (glass slats) which dont really help the street noise and heat that you get althroughout waikiki - if you can sleep with aircon on its worth doing it. Shower was dark when curtain pulled which was a pain. Small room - ok for one maybe 2 but no more.Other Breakfast is only available in tight range of times and not suitable times to get out to the attractions early (ie arizona you need to be there before 7.30 so means you will miss breakfast as first delivery is 7.30)No resturant, mini bar or room service - not major as there are things close Pool is small and was closed 1 of the 2 days i was there but again no consequence Parking - i didnt have a car but looked a bit of a hassle. For whatever reason this is not that well known a hotel so make sure you have the address handy for taxis etc as a lot dont recognise the name.

<Author>HappySurfer
<Content>Not for "Pool People" If you want a nice pool, don't stay here . The Pool was not an issue for us, we walked to the beach, and were very happy at the Aloha Surf. The Front Desk will provide Beach Towels on request. We booked a Superior room, it was nicely furnished and clean. The Refrigerator and Microwave looked new. No bugs! Although the Bathroom was not new, it was clean and reasonably well maintained. The bed was firm and comfortable. We slept well once we discovered how to stop the wind from rattling our door (we used a hand towel to steady the door against the tradewinds)- and of course run the Air Conditioner to drown out Kuhio street noise. The A/C unit looked new, and performed flawlessly.The staff were helpful with our requests. Parking can be difficult in the area, but we only rented a car for three days and found parking for $15.00. We walked or took the bus most of the time. The Housekeepers are a bit quirky, and some days the room was cleaned more thoroughly than others, but we always had clean towels and TP. When I walked into the huge beach resort hotels, I was glad to be staying at the Aloha Surf. If you want a giant resort hotel with lots of service and amenities, this is not the hotel for you. We found it to be a good value, and may return again in the future.

<Author>chanbru
<Content>Nice place to sleep after a day in the beach We stayed at the Aloha Surf that now is called Aqua Aloha Surf Hotel. The place looked decent in the pictures and the deal was good. We spent 7 nights over there. At first, I thought the room with a queen bed in the 2nd floor was too small. It was basically 15ft x 15ft (including the bath -no bath tub, closet and the furnitues). It was too tiny for 2 adults walking among luggages that I called the front desk. They said my reservation was for a standard room and it was the best I could get because the hotel was booked up. They offered us an upgrade for $20/night. After the 1st night, we decided to stay in the same tiny room because we realized we were out most of the time and coming back only for sleeping. The room has an adequate closet size, builky new furnitures, a cooler, safe box,alarm clock and a flat screen TV. The room was renovated and was confortable despite the size. Internet is available at the looby (wireless, but it did not work for my laptop for some reason) and DSL wired at the room (but you have to have a cable for it). The breakfast was delivered in the room every morning and it was a small muffin, yogurt and canned juice for each adult. Not much of food, but better than nothing. The hotel is surrounded by nice places for breakfast starting on $3.99 and good restaurants for dinner and lunch. Check the PERRY'S SMORGY restaurant one block from the hotel. Excellent deals on Buffet with simple but good food. The hotel is also located 2 blocks away from Waikiki Beach. Be prepared to know where you are going because the front desk is always busy and has no time to answer inquiries and give suggestions. I found that some of the staff was not knowledgeable of the vicinities, but nothing I couldn't find using the free internet. Overall, it was a pleasant stay. It was a good deal for the money spent. No luxuries, I admit. If you have a lot of things planned, you will not even bothered by the little inconveniences at the hotel. Like i said before, the place is excellent for sleeping after a day full of fun. All you need is a confortable bed to crash on. Another thing I liked is the coin laundry at teh basement. Very convenient. Would I stay there again? SUre I would.

<Author>JKDM
<Content>Just Adequate! I booked our family vacation at the Aloha Surf after reading the hotel description on Expedia, i.e., completely renovated in late 2005, with new furnishings and bathrooms. My first impression was mild disappointment! While the room and the reception area were decent and looked exactly like the pictures on Expedia, there was a musty smell noticeable in the hallways and in the room. We stayed in a deluxe unit which had a twin bed, a double bed and a pull out couch, and there was a bar with a microwave and a small fridge. Yes, the furniture and the bar seemed fairly new and there was a flat screen TV, but the complete renovation of the room seemed like a half-hearted attempt and did not seem to include the bathroom. We had to ask to move to another room because the first room we were in the bathroom was unacceptable! There was so much mold in the grout of the tiled shower that my daughter and I had to wear our sandals to take showers and we tried to make it as quickly as possible! And to make things even worse, there was a faint smell of urine. The second room we were in was better but still the shower did not show any renovations. The positives of this hotel were the location and the staff. We were close to the beach - about 2 blocks away - and practically walked everywhere we wanted to go. The area seemed safe enough that my daughter and I were out and about up to midnight. There is a number of restaurants around, Chili's, IHOP, Denny's, as well as many smaller family-run places. There is a Food Pantry and an ABC store right around the corner. The cab fare from the airport was about $32.00 plus tip. The staff was very friendly and accommodating, from the front desk to the housekeeping department. Every morning there was a continental breakfast delivered to our room at the time of our choosing, and it was always on time. The breakfast was just a muffin, yogurt and a can of fruit juice, but it was a nice touch and nicely presented in a little basket. Overall, it was an adequate place but I think the description on Expedia was misleading. For all the good points about the Aloha Surf, I don't think I will consider coming back here for our next vacation in Oahu.

<Author>Lemonade1
<Content>Decent for the price I am sitting in our room at the Aloha Surf, having stayed here 3 nights (leaving tomorrow). I booked this room because of the free internet access and the reviews on this page. (We had just come from the Kauai Marriott--Fantastic place but they charged $13/day for internet access!!) For the price, this is a decent place to stay, including a small breakfast and the convenience of fridge and microwave. Our room is an odd combination of old (dated wallpaper, the shower is only slightly scary, popcorn ceiling, concrete lanai that is good for drying your wet clothing) and new (internet access--cable is provided but I brought my own--, flat screen TV, granite sink countertop). The carpet and furniture in this room are not new, not old, and comfortable enough. I stayed with my 2 teen daughters, and the room is small but fine for us--a double bed (on the small side for 2 people), a twin, and a fold out couch which we did not use for sleeping. I like having the separate couch/coffee table area for computer use. The microwave, in room coffee, and small fridge I thought we would use a lot more than we did, because food in the area is convenient and inexpensive. Breakfast is an average size muffin, a cup of yogurt, and a 12 ounce can of juice, which was okay for us. We did not use the tiny pool and opted for the beach. The hotel provides beach towels. The service at the desk is okay, not terribly friendly but we didn't need much. The location is great--a short 2 block walk to the beach, 1 1/2 block from the back entrance the the international marketplace. The Food Pantry is a full size grocery store on the same block, open till 1am. If you want a resort vacation, this is not the place; if you want a clean, no frills place in a great location to base your day, I would recommend the Aloha Surf.

<Author>OandO
<Content>Good location. Decent price. No frills The location of the hotel is 2 blocks from Waikiki beach and a few blocks from the International Market Place, which is in the heart of the Waikiki action. The room was okay. The beds were a bit soft. I got the Deluxe room which included a twin bed, a double, and a double size (or maybe it was Queen size) sofa bed. The mini kitchen came with a small refridgerator (the kind you have in your dorm room) a sink, and a small microwave. The pool is 5-8 feet deep and a bit bigger than a normal sized hot tub. The shower had some mold at the top and there was no bath tub. They provide a continental breakfast in the AM, which is delivered to your room. There's highspeed internet access (via a CAT 5 cable) for free in your room or free wireless in the lobby. The staff was efficient but not overly friendly and probably a bit overworked. We were not allowed to park in the garage below the hotel for the first night because they were all booked up. So, they told us to park at the Waikiki Banyan, about a 7 minute walk away.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>We'll be back!! My husband and I stayed at Aston Aloha Aqua Surf for seven days and it definitely exceeded our expectations! It was perfect for us. We got the hotel as part of a Suntrips package, so we weren't sure what to expect. The hotel just finished extensive renovations into a very cool boutique 'surfer' hotel with all new furnishings and landscaping. We stayed on the 9th floor and had an excellent view of the canal on one side and the ocean on the other. The room had tasteful furnishings and photographs and wall hangings and everything was brand new. The location was perfect being only two blocks from main street Kuhio so it was easy walking distance to the beach, surfing, dinner, drinks, shopping, etc. The room was spotless and well lit (lots of windows) and the beds were very comfortable and they provided a microwave and a coffee machine and an in-room safe and internet connection and the AC worked well. The rooms are definitely on the small side so I don't recommend more than 2 per room. However, if you are the type of travelers who like to hang out at the hotel all day and use room service and use the pool this is not the place for you - you would be happier at a larger hotel such as the Marriott or the Hyatt. The lobby is large and spacious with surfer videos showing all day on wall-mounted flat screens, but the hotel definitely is on the small side and is not really designed for hanging out. But if you want a very nice and inexpensive place to sleep when we're not playing on the island, then it will be perfect for you. Other notes: Hotel is very safe since all access is through the main lobby. Parking is $14 a day so be prepared for that. Breakfast was very minimal but there are great breakfast restaurants less than a block away. Other reviews mentioned this being a bad part of town, but it seemed just fine to us. We did see maybe 2 or 3 prostitutes during our entire stay, but I think they're everywhere in Waikiki after 10pm. Waikiki has a lot to do and is very active, so it can also be noisy at night. The noise can be remedied by closing the window or staying near the top floors or as a last resort bring earplugs. But if you need a really quiet place to stay I would recommend staying out of Waikiki and staying in a BB in Kailua on the beach.Have fun!

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Better than I expected; not too shabby I visited Honolulu eights months ago, and I made sure to research hotels before deciding where to stay. I would have liked to have been in a hotel that's on the beach, but I didn't want to pay the higher prices; plus, we were in Hawaii for the outdoors more than the indoors. After researching for a few weeks, I decided on reserving a room at the Aston Aloha Surf. A few of the reviews didn't seem positive about this place, but some reviewers stated it was just fine. First off, I was surprised at how nice the lobby area looked, compared to the internet photos. We arrived at the hotel a few hours before check-in, so the person who checked us in, allowed us to keep our luggage (with other travelers' luggage) in a storage closet, until we returned from a close walk to Waikiki beach. Once we went up to our 7th floor room, I was surprised at how clean the hallways were. The room looked as if it were recently renovated, with a nice comfortable bed (room was not too big, but not too small), clean floors, small refrigerator, cable tv, and night stands. The only thing I didn't like was the outdated bathroom, which has a shower (no tub; which is alright). We did not pay for a lanai (balcony), but we were given one at no extra charge. Since we had the lanai (our room faced towards the east), we had perfect sunrise views, views of Diamond Head, the streets below and of the ocean. Not a bad place to stay for the money. The hotel is only 2 long blocks to the ocean, and we walked a few times. Enterprise Rental car is a few blocks west of the hotel, so that was very convenient. The Alawai Canal is across the street. When I go back to Waikiki Beach, and if I don't care about being in a hotel on the beach, I'll stay there again. Being there for 4 nights and 5 days, and only spending $550 apiece, was super cheap. Good place.

<Author>capndrake
<Content>Don't be afraid of this hotel We were looking for a budget hotel that was clean and this place exceeded our expectations. The room (6th floor) was completely renovated, new furniture, carpeting,a/c, fridge, M/W, coffeemaker, and very expensive bronze art on the wall. At first, I was only hopeful that we wouldn't have the problems that other guests experienced, but this place was delightful. We called a week earlier for a non-smoking room and got an answering machine oh-oh, so called the booking agent, Travelocity, who called for us to ensure a non-smoking room. Within two hours, the manager also called us back to ensure our non-smoking room.  If you want large rooms, good restaurants, security police, go to the Hilton and pay three times the rate. If you don't want to see cockroaches and hookers, stay away from Waikiki. I never saw a roach, but you've got to wade through the hookers to get back to any hotel in Waikiki, and as the night gets late, say after 10 pm, their pimps force them to accost any male. This hotel is one block off the main drag, Kuhio, so they don't hang around here, but once you get up to Kuhio around King's Village, watch out. Other plusses--1 block from only supermarket in Waikiki, 1 block from ABC store but everything is, short walk to main Waikiki beach, Intl Marketplace, and all the activities. Minuses--rather chintzy included breakfast (Coffee not bad), almost as chintzy as I was in looking for a price, rooms certainly not big enough for more than two, Waikiki street noise had to be remedied by earplugs, but I've stayed in many hotels in this class here and have had the same problem. Last problem, if you decide to rent a car, you'll pay $$ to store it for the night in Waikiki. The concierge here was good enough to give us a couple of places to see about car storage, since they were renovating their own parking garage which is nowhere near big enough for their guests and employees. One was $7 per night, with in an out privileges for 24 hours. Bottom line, we'd return in a second.

<Author>sallyglam
<Content>Spectacular vacation and a fantastic budget hotel! I stayed at the Aloha Surf with a friend and found it to fit our needs fine. Some people seem overly picky when writing their reviews. Its no Sheraton Moana but I can't stay at the Sheraton for $59 - If you want Sheraton style...you have to spend the money.We were upgraded to the 16th floor, which had a great view of both the canal and water/city side. Paper was delivered daily (but who's reading the paper when you're in Hawaii?). Continental breakfast wasn't our thing - too much white bread and fatty stuff - easy fix - hit the ABC and bought fruit and yogurt. Staff was friendly, helpful and we had no issues. Room was cleaned daily - no critters - excellent a/c - fantastic for a two star. It's going under renovations this summer, so I can only imagine that it'll be even nicer by the fall.I would without a doubt stay here again. If you're going on your honeymoon or looking for high scale - don't bother with the Surf. If you are looking for a fun vacation in a good location with reasonable rates and a clean place to sleep - the Surf is perfect.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Wouldn't recommend We stayed at the Aloha Surf for the last two days of our second honeymoon/25th anniversary trip. We walked in in the afternoon, and we were immediately greeted by an argument between a woman staying at the hotel, who was having problem with a key card, which evidently hadn't worked on three different occasions. She was livid, even threatening to jump back there and start tearing up that computer! The manager came out, and fixed her problem. We asked if we could see the room before we signed anything, and were given the key to a room which smelled strongly of smoke, and looked dirty. We told the clerk that the room was totally unacceptable, so we were given another key to check out another room. Upon initial inspection, we decided that it was too late in the day to change hotels, and it would suffice for two nights. The room was small and had too much furniture in it (a double bed and a twin, when one king would have been great, and given the room more space). The carpet was nasty, the sink had a rusty faucet. a cracked sink, and an air conditioner that even out-noised the traffic in the street.When we asked about a bellman, we were told that there wasn't one. Okay, we can deal with that. They did have a bell cart, which we were allowed to use. THEN, the real problem. We were asked if we had a car, which we did, having rented one. We were told that there was NO parking at all, none, despite all advertisements saying that there was paid parking available. We were told that we could park at a public lot about 15 minutes away, and walk back to the hotel!! We stated our dissatisfaction politely, and asked to speak to someone about getting transferred to another hotel, with parking. After a few minutes, a very nice man named David came out saying that he was the hotel manager. He asked to speak to us, and showed us where he would allow us to park - in his personal parking space. He explained that he had workers coming every day, and that was why the parking was so limited. David was the only good thing about this hotel, though we didn't complain about anything else, because the parking situation was such a major issue.Every morning we were awakened at 7:30 by the sound of hammering and banging. The room was not inviting, and just a bit creepy. It needs a new paint job, the curtains have holes in them, the carpet is dirty and the room is just too small. The advertisements I had read online before our trip stated it had been completely renovated, but they are in the process of renovation - a clerk told us that the top two floors were done, and they were working their way down. The lobby is lovely, but there it ends. Nothing else about this hotel is appealing - save the possiblity that because David is the manager, things will get better. He is a wonderful, caring man, but in all likelihood can only do what he is allowed to do. He saved the end of vacation from being a disaster, but could only do so much. The room was disappointing on all levels.I would never recomend this hotel, despite the efforts on David's part.

<Author>TinaYoung
<Content>You get what you paid for Because I was planning on staying in Hawaii for ten days after visiting LA, I wanted to try to save some money on hotels. The rooms were very decently sized (with an area for couch and coffee table) and had a wet bar with a mini-fridge microwave. My only complaints were that the carpets were dirty looking, the room was a little dark (even for a corner unit), the air conditioner barely worked (it was lukewarm air blowing out), and every morning we woke up to the sound of the wind. We were on a very high floor and on the corner as well, so every morning we were woken up by the roaring sound of the wind... we laughed about it, saying it sounded like we were in a wind-tunnel, but stopped laughing after the third morning. Otherwise, it's a convenient location for a cheap price, so just ask to stay on a lower floor.

<Author>ToniVitanza
<Content>We loved the Aloha Surf Just got back yesterday (November 28, 2004) from a stay at the Aston Aloha Surf Hotel. I cannot say enough good things about this hotel and its staff. I want to say upfront that I am a 44-year-old flight attendant with less than a decade of experience. I have used my flight privileges extensively, but before joining the airline I traveled a great deal as a student and journalist and stayed in ALL kinds of places. I am anything but a spoiled traveler. (I trained English teachers in Poland in one of several previous lives, for goodness sakes! You can't imagine what a Stalinist hotel looks like when it hasn't seen maintenance in 20 years.) I read the opinions here -- every last one of them -- and the only one that made me think twice about booking at the Aloha Surf was the guy from Marin County who said the Marriott in Stockton, California was nicer. Well, I lived in the Bay Area at one time and I would guess his house in Marin is probably nicer that a lot of hotels I'd be thrilled to sleep in, so maybe he should just stay at his house next time he needs a vacation. Since visiting the hotel I am even more inclined to think he is just another spoiled traveler. (Or just spoiled.)I have stayed at several Astons in the islands, including the Honolulu Prince in Waikiki (wonderful if you're on a real tight budget) and the Pacific Monarch (nice if you want to splurge, enjoy a rooftop hot tub, and want a separate bedroom away from your kids) and at the Maui Lu outside Kihei in Maui. I will admit that I began staying there because they offered a rate for airline employees, but I'll say here that I don't believe my rate at the Aloha Surf was substantially less than published rack rates, and I think you can trust my opinions. (I have raked hotels over the coals in this forum even when they practically gave the room away to airline employees.) I have lost count of the number of times I have visited Waikiki since 1997 (my first visit).The hotel's location is FANTASTIC for access on foot to everything in Waikiki. It is also near bus and trolley stops and a taxi stand is on the block.We are aware that mornings are noisy in Waikiki. The beach is surrounded by a concrete canyon of high-rise hotels; yes, the garbage trucks and delivery trucks make noise. But generally mainlanders are awake by that time anyway. Waikiki is NOT a resort; it is more like the Vegas strip parallel to a beach with really great landscaping and no casinos. So we don't -- and you shouldn't -- expect peace and quiet. That's another part of Oahu, or another island altogether. Read guidebooks instead of relying on some postcard fantasy of what Waikiki really is.My husband (age 64) WANTED a street-facing room because he is a college professor who goes to Waikiki for the street vibe, the noise, the excitement, seeing people walk by at all hours. It was still not THAT noisy. Without our even asking, Helene (a beautiful woman who works the front desk -- Helene, why can't you come work for my airline? I need more colleagues like you) granted us an upgrade to Room 1201. It contained a double bed, a twin bed and a sofa sleeper that could have held two more reasonably-sized adults. We put our 11-year-old son in the twin bed and enjoyed sitting on the sofa and reading our complimentary paper in the mornings, when we weren't sitting on the balcony watching the moonlight, the sunrise, the lights of Waikiki come on or go out. The room was positively IMMACULATE. The mini-frig and microwave, big TV (with cable) and wallpaper and carpeting were all apparently brand new. The cabinetry had been repainted, the sink was shiny and the water pressure was strong and water always hot. The AC was on and the room cooled to 69 when we walked in. My only suggestion would be to replace the rather worn and narrow curtain in the shower stall. (There is no tub.) Yes, the towels might be thin, but the wonderful maid (who introduced herself by name, shook our hands, bowed, and explained very apologetically on Wednesday that we would not see her again until Saturday because she would be off until then) would give you as many stacks of them as you wanted. (And there were substitute maids until Saturday; from the regular maid's apologies we thought there might not be!) There are dishes and dishtowels and cutlery and a coffee pot, mugs and plastic cups and even a couple of pkgs. of coffee to make your own if you wish. There is a complimentary continental breakfast downstairs (near the small but beautifully maintained pool; how big does it need to be for you to rinse the sand off your body?) beginning at 7 am. They have coffee, several flavors of mini muffins, very very good mini croissants, breads, OJ and passion/mango/guava juice which I LOVE. (It is great with rum or vodka; bring a bottle with you and buy a carton of juice at the Food Pantry, a 24-hr. supermarket whose back parking lot is next door to the Aloha Surf. Grab a made-to-order deli sandwich, bottle of wine, beer or booze there too; also sushi to go and fresh fruit. A carton of eggs and some tortillas made the heartier breakfast my son needs and all I needed was one of the small bowls and fork that were provided, and the microwave. I had a papaya on my balcony every morning before going down for the official breakfast and they were 79 cents a pound at the Food Pantry.)During my stay I needed to email my airline and started to use the pay-for-use computer in the corner; the hotel lobby staff stopped me and warned me how inconsistently it worked. They directed me right across the street to an internet cafe where, for the $2 a Starbucks bottled cappucino cost, I got free use of the internet. There was safe in the room; we did not use it and did not get charged for it. Like every place, you had to sign a waiver. This is just defensive hospitality, it is not unusual.Some general tips for first-time visitors: Do not take the shuttle from the airport; it is the same price as a taxi ride and you have to stop at everyone else's hotel along the way.Take the number 22 or 58 bus for $2 to Diamond Head and hike up to the crater. It costs a buck to get in and $2 for the certificate at the top. Wear good shoes and socks and carry water and a camera and a cellphone so you can call home and leave yourself a message!We never fail to have breakfast at least one morning at the Pacific Beach Hotel, a very short walk from the Aloha Surf. This is the first place we ever stayed in Waikiki because we were attending an academic conference. The hotel is overpriced, we think, but breakfast in the Oceanarium is not to be missed. Go hungry...preferably before your hike up Diamond Head. My husband always wants to visit Duke's Canoe Club for happy hour and I always send folks to Iolani Palace in downtown Waikiki. Be sure to watch the video before your tour. Take your picture next to the statue of Duke. Every Friday night there are fireworks over the water (and there were on Thanksgiving night too) and the second Sunday of every month Waikiki shuts down for a food festival you will not want to miss. Splurge at the bar called House Without A Key; it is at the Halekulani Hotel (one of the most expensive in the world) but at House Without a Key you will enjoy the best Kona coffee, cocktails and coconut shrimp on earth while listening to a Grammy-winning band play Hawaiian tunes and watching Miss Hawaii hula dance. Worth every penny while you watch the sunset over the waves. If you're from the mainland you will wake up early and go to sleep early; do not cheat yourself by trying to acclimate to the time change (unless you're staying a long while, you never will). As soon as you wake up, GET UP; early morning in Waikiki is the best time to walk down the street or down the beach. Wander through the gardens in front of the Royal Hawaiian hotel (the pink one); they are incredible. To conclude about the hotel: If you let anything on this website sway you to stay away, you will be missing out and probably paying too much. We three agreed that is THE place for our next family honeymoon (that is what we call our vacations) and it is hands-down the choice for our next visit. (Spring break?) THANK YOU ASTON and the staff at the ALOHA SURF HOTEL.

<Author>Ninjagirrl
<Content>Had a ball! I just returned from a 6-day visit, (Nov 10-16) and I had a wonderful time. I must say that I was nervous because of some of the reviews I read about this hotel. But I realized quickly that every hotel I researched (a whole lot) had some good reviews and some bad reviews. For starters if you are on a budget (like me) this is a great hotel. My room was clean and decent. It was fine for 2 people. The rooms are small-ish, but I found that to be the case at a lot of the hotels in Honolulu. Some of the complaints I read about in the past I realized were quite anal when I finally saw things for myself, such as: the noise level from the street- ok-there is noise, but this is Waikiki! People are walking, driving and just plain outside all of the time! If street noise bothers you then you should never leave the muffled safety of your house. The prostitutes-ok-well I have never been to a city that didn't have them!, The no-frills of the hotel-well I went to Oahu to see the island not to sit in my hotel room and contemplate on the thread-count of the sheets. I had a clean room, plenty of fresh, clean towels, a shower, toilet, sink, fridge, tv (which I turned on maybe twice), coffeemaker, safe, and a lanai with a decent view. Continental breakfast was cool, donuts, muffins, croissant, fruit, coffee  juice. A store in the lobby, Foodland next door(grocerystore), Zippy's, Burger King, Pizza Hut all within 1-2 blocks,ABC store on the corner, and best of all a short walk to the beach and all the shops! I came on a hotel budget-meaning I would rather spend my money shopping, dinner, clubbing, sightseeing and fun stuff, than spending it on a grossly overpriced room that I pretty much only plan to sleep and shower in, like most everyone, I just need it to be clean and safe! I had a wonderful time and I would stay at this hotel again. If you need to surround your self in luxury for the 8-10 hours your eyes are closed at night, go to the Hyatt or somewhere else ridiculously priced like that. (what? are the towels fluffier?your just drying off, relax)The staff was nice and courteous also. Had a good time and I am going back in February. Can't wait. (I did stay away from the Parrot guy tho, thanks to all the tips on that here, I saw him harangue a lot of people)

<Content>Just as good as the 1st time! Astons staff eager to please! My son and I were late to check in but it was due to the very overcrowded Alamo renta car! <Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>decent with a great location The Aston Aloha Surf is a great choice for those who want to stay in a decent, clean and affordable hotel that is walking distance to Waikiki beach, restaurants, shopping, shows etc. There is a 24 hour grocery store right next to it, and it is about a 5-7 minute walk from the beach and in the middle of the tourist district. The rooms a fairly small but you won't want to spend too much time there anyways. The pool is a joke, but who goes to Hawaii and swims in a pool? The rates are pretty good and the room I had a balcony with a great view, cable tv, great air conditioning, a safe, a microwave and a fridge. I had an amazing time with my boyfriend on a vacation Sept 2-9th 2004. This hotel is good for the economically conscious who want a really great stay.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>needs improvement The hotel was nice but it needs some improvements. There was a tiny room air conditioner only in the room and to get any air to where the bed was I had to have a fan in the room. The headboards for the bed need to be bolted either to the beds or to the wall. Every time any one in the next room made any kind of movements on the bed the headboard would bang up against the wall waking me up. Also I do not know when they last cleaned the filter in the air conditioner it was filthy. If any one from the hotel reads this go and clean all of the filters in your rooms, it does not take that long. The rest of the hotel was nice and clean. The location was great, with in walking distance to many things. The staff that I dealt with was great and helpful no problems with them. Very promt in response to the few little things that I asked about. The maid who cleaned my room was great, real friendly. Thank you for everything.

<Author>Tommy2pdx
<Content>One Could Do Better For The Money Spent a long 4 day weekend here a coupla years back and my feeling is Never again!. While the outside and lobby appear aesthetically pleasing, the rooms themselves (at least the one we had) were shabby. Why was Waikiki built with so much cinderblock? Admittedly, we booked a short time ahead and got a budget class room but that shouldn't mean an experience that's shortchanged. We got what I am sure was their dumpiest room on the 3rd floor that had 2 Murphy beds and a carpet whose color reminded me of baby puke. The bathroom was microscopic. Other negatives: parking was 10.00 a day in slots so narrow it took a shoehorn to squeeze into, street noise, flimsy louvred windows, a pathetic pool and THE LONGEST WAITS for an elevator that I have ever endured. We finally gave up and used the stairs....probably a good thing as the exercise would do one good. Positives: a grocery store right next door, easy access to H-1 and plentiful variety of restaurants along Kuhio. If you stay here, caveat emptor! You can do better for your hard earned dollar.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Aston Aloha Surf is Excellent Aloha! Carla here~~ Should you find yourself staying here, I hope you find all the Aloha many of us happy guests at, The Aston Aloha Surf have ;-) ... It was by mistake we ended up staying at the Aston Aloha Surf, but one I would surely do again...Where I wanted to stay was all booked, well into August...I was scrambling for a place, at the last hours...I researched and researched, but wasn't finding anything, and then I ran across one of the best mistakes I have yet made! ;-) Upon our arrival, we were greeted by a real sweet man (sorry I have forgotten your name) (Lance)? You were so sweet and had a country-mile-wide smile; you let me check out 3 different rooms, before I made up my mind ;-) Our room was more than I expected after reading the many negative comments about The Aston Aloha Surf ~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~We stayed in room 801 05/19/04, and sadly left May 28, 04 ;-( ... I almost questioned myself about noise levels (It was almost too quiet) -- Having lived on Kuhio Ave. in 1982 (2465 Kuhio), I had expected there might be some noise...After a long flight from Sioux City, Iowa via Minneapolis (8 plus hours) ~~ I was quite pleased to stand in a hot shower for a good 20 minutes at least~~Each morning I had a great shower, as well as a few at night...(loved the water pressure~~That is very important to me, since I love hard pounding water, and soft flowing, too--one can get several flows from the shower head--which was real nice) ... My honey loved his showers, as well ;-) We smelled only our sweet lei's for the first few nights, and then, had our candle going when in our room and getting comfy, after many fun long days and romantic evenings, of enjoying beautiful Oahu ;-) My honey still has his first packet of Kona coffee we received the first day (we are saving it)...I brought coffee along (which we never even used--IMO, A good hint for guests who don't want to buy coffee while there (after the first night) at the wonderful Aston Aloha Surf ;-) It is true the kitchenette is very small, but we didn't really need it, with Perry's Smorgasbord just a good softball throw, (or maybe that's a Sammy home-run) towards the Ocean, from the front steps of the Aston Aloha Surf. (Perry's, Very reasonably priced, tasty, and a pleasant atmosphere--Waterfalls, candles, etc.) 9.95 for Dinner or Supper as Ken calls it...I challenge anyone to say that they can't get enough filling food or find something very tasty there--in other words, Perry's gets a 4 from this ole gal;-) The hotel staff was more than accommodating during our stay. One night I did laundry well into the wee hours; The laundry area (which is in the basement) is opened 24 hours and one uses a key to enter the small tidy area, making it a relatively safe place to do laundry late at night, or in the wee hours of the morning--There's 2 W machines and 2 dryers, I believe--Both 1.25 to use--I suggest going to (The Grocery Outlet 1199 Dillingham Blvd) which sells frozen and canned foods as well as housewares, health and beauty care products, and other such items--yet, not in bulk like other discount stores, but individual sizing, etc. -- And, there's (Price Busters 1505 Dillingham Blvd) too, for checking out reasonable prices for your laundry soap (I bought a bottle for 1.00 and left most of it in the room ;-) -- I brought along fabric softener sheets to keep our luggage smelling fresh, and for laundry I anticipated might need to be done...The Grocery Outlet would be for checking out the reasonable prices for food (if you plan to use your kitchenette) --- There's also a store not far from The Grocery Outlet that has a 10 dollar annual fee, with many great buys...Can't think of the name of it, but ask a local, they'll tell you where it is ... Another tip: Instead of buying block ice for days you may plan to spend a day at another beach or another area on the island, freeze an empty juice or milk carton, and that will work well in your ice chest, it's less messy, and will leave you with cold water, should that become necessary ;-) ~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~In the wee hours of doing laundry, I had a great conversation with the neatest lady. (Nikki, thank you so much for putting up with me, and turning me on to Hawaii's (IZ of Hawaii) Your Aloha spirit will live with me always! ... I know I have spelled your name incorrectly, but you know I know, you are one special lady!!! I do hope you enjoy the little song thing I put together for you on my webpage about your most wonderful hotel and excellent hospitality from the whole hotel Staff! ;-) Mahalo!!!~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~We had no problem at all with our air conditioner--Kept it at 60 degrees and actually had to turn it off a couple times ;-)~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~Many have remarked about about how small the rooms are at The Aston Aloha Surf ... Ken and I are not newlyweds~~ However, being in a smallish room (not that small--if you know Waikiki) We felt like newlyweds, I must say, ;-) ... We never used the pool; (I did look at it one morning after our daily free continental breakfast, and the pool looked very clean and inviting) We were lucky to hit the beach just one day the whole duration (went to Kailua Bay Beach--A very pretty beach--check it out, is my suggestion) ... We were too busy driving around the Island; I had to show Ken the Leeward side where I lived in Nanakuli, Makaha, and things from the past, that most tours won't take you to or show you ;-) If you are renting a car-the garage is easy to get in and out of, we never had any problems, and we were in a Grand-Am, -- true the parking is 8.00 a day but that is also true for most of Waikiki--and many hotels costs more than 8.00...Renting a car one can check out the Leeward side, all the way to the last beach (As far as one can go--just a little past that) IMO, The Leeward Side is not only interesting, but has some of the prettier beaches IMO, and there is an excellent golf course in Makaha Valley...There's also an interesting cave almost at the end of that side, with a marker across the street that explains a little about the cave ;-) ... That cave saved my life back in 1982--Long story ... I was real happy to read the marker that is now across the street; I now believe I know why the cave was my protector way back when...There's a lot of interesting history all throughout Oahu, ancient folklore, taboo's etc. --- Locals are happy to talk about such things if you ask them ;-)~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~One night while walking down the main street ---The one by the beach--We were lucky to watch a man with beautiful McCaw's, and a beautiful young lady holding 4 or 5 of them; maybe it was 6 very colorful birds...Ken held a brilliant green one, which fell asleep on his finger ;-) ... The fascinating experience found me chatting with a very nice couple...Strangely, the man knew my ex--The friendly tourist worked for World Airways when World Airways was still in Oakland, Ca. (My ex was W. A. Stores Super/they knew one another because of that)... That couple had to leave in the morning; I sure enjoyed talking with them, and talking about Bob. Bob is with God now (1991)...That was really neat crossing their path and sharing our journeys! That is something that is really neat about Oahu, IMO--All the people one meets, all the journeys traveled, and shared ;-) Many fine people shared their wonderful experiences with us, with respect to the Aston Aloha Surf and other things Oahu~~Belle, if you ever read this, it was a real pleasure meeting another happy guest from The Aston Aloha Surf--Hope you made it to the airport on time! ;-) For all of you lucky enough to stay in room 801, as you well know, it does in fact face the street~~ We never heard any noises that woke us up or disturbed us. I had no clue the walls are hear through walls; hope we didn't offend anyone, hehe ;-0 ... We would definitely stay again! IMO, Spend the extra money one would have to spend (for a room on the beach, or across the street from the beach) to enjoy lasting heartprints you'll cherish always, is my thinking! ;-) ~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~We never waited 15 minutes for either elevator--There are two, that is true...Actually, when they were a little slow (which wasn't very often) we'd get in an extra kiss, breather, or remember something we may have forgotten had we been rushing. In Hawaii, Take it Easy, Enjoy, Hang Lose ... That's my thinking ;-)~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~I would like to suggest something to any family of 4...Where I was going to stay is a real decent place IMO, and has plenty of room for a family of 4, IMO...It varies on the price, but averages around 600. for a week per suite (different people own units in the Condo) There are several webpage's on this particular Condo. However, They are booked well in advance, I learned! I have stayed there (past tense) with my Mother and a young lady (friend) ... Each unit has it's own full kitchen/dishwasher/full frige/WD/FREE parking/many things not at the Aloha Surf; The units IMO, are great for a family, or guests who like to stay in (more or less) or cook, etc. ... You will not find the Aloha Spirit there that you find at The Aloha Surf, unless it's different now, and or you totally make your own/That's always a good possibility, too ;-)...There is a guard at the front desk area (A very small area) They have a nice pool, and barbecue area, if it's still the same as in 98 or 99...I have omitted the name so as to not break any guidelines with this write-up~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~I did LOL about the curtains at The Aston Aloha Surf...I noticed that ours gave us a light show, hehe ... But, like I told Ken, If I was going to stay in during the day, why be in Hawaii on vacation? ;-)...It just added to the sweet uniqueness of the Aloha Surf--When I did notice the peculiar light show (one early morning, I realized I wasting time sleeping ;-) ... ~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~We had a wonderful stay at the Aston Aloha Surf ... Great people and I have only Mahalo's for all of our hosts and the excellent staff, etc. ... I only wish it was longer! The thing we liked most about the Aloha Surf is the such happy-go-lucky smiling hosts, ~~ Location, location, (Close to the beach, restaurants, shopping, excitement, etc.) ~~ and the continental breakfast hits the spot for coffee, juice, muffins, toast, etc. (I only went twice; Ken went every morning/I'm a night owl--too early for me-7-9 AM?)...There at The Aston Aloha Surf lives a special feeling of true Aloha in the air!--It is a pleasant motel for the money, no doubt! ... If you are going to be driven anywhere, rent a car (which I highly recommend as previously noted) ... The reason I highly recommend driving yourself, are at least two fold...The Bus is slow, and impersonal, and it doesn't go to some of the more remarkable places, like the last beach on the Leeward side...I think The Bus only goes as far as Makaha Valley Plantation--I could be mistaken, too...I know it takes a long time to get there via The Bus...The bus is slow, oftentimes very crowded, and at best, it's difficult to take along all the things one might want to take for a daily discovery adventure, such as beach wear, ice chests, etc., not to mention any shopping one might do (finding treasures along the highways and byways of beautiful Oahu ;-) And, if you are a smoker, why put yourself through all that, too? ;-)Anyway, Try driving out of a Beach front Motel parking place to go somewhere on/from Kalakaua Avenue, (if you find a parking space--and forget what it will cost per night to park--much more than the Aloha Surf)---eeks ... And, if you are out of shape like we are, try walking to Kuhio Beach from a hotel on the end of the beach where it begins from the Ala Moana End--where many of the more expensive hotels are ;-) (Kuhio Beach, being the beach I prefer--it's better for swimming, and watching the young ones catch a wave, etc., IMO)... I could write and write why the Aloha Surf is one of the better places to stay for a short stay, IMO, but this is plenty long...I will be updating my noncommercial webpage soon (personal page about my experience at The Aston Aloha Surf)... More tips, etc. -- Keep in mind, To each his or her own ... I think we all have different reasons and taste, so who am I to say that one might be a happy or unhappy guest if one stays at The Aston Aloha Surf--I think it is sad to NOT just enjoy and be happy to be in paradise!!! ;-) Mahalo!Thanks again Nikki, for making our Stay even more special than it already was...I love listening to Hawaii's IZ of Hawaii ... You were right!!! For anyone reading this, If you like my Aloha Surf personal noncommercial webpage, you'll love and feel the Aloha Spirit at The Aston Aloha Surf ;-) I would love for you to sign the guest book on my webpage, if you stayed at the Aston Aloha Surf~~Especially, if you stayed in room 801...Or just sign it if you stayed in Oahu or want to, etc. ;-)In Wyoming (several years ago), this motel had a guest book in the room (one in each room) and called them a dream book--I thought that was so neat! It was real interesting to read where people were from, their travels/journey, and what was on their mind, etc. ... I believe that is what I love most about the Concrete Jungle of Ohau--One gets to meet and mingle with folk from all over the world, everyday, and everyday it's someone different, usually. Ha! -- Though it's a mass of concrete, it's always alive with all of our dreams, and the Aloha in the air, if we just look for it, and do it, IMO--Which IMO, is all found at The Aston Aloha Surf ;-) Oh, and the weather--that's just an added bonus!!!IZ of Hawaii says it all, Somewhere Over The Rainbow/What a Wonderful World...Mahalo to all at The Aloha Surf!!!I would list my URL listed but maybe that would cause my write-up to be unacceptable? I just don't know, so I won't put it in this write-up ... Sincerely,Ken  Carla, Very happy guests of The Aston Aloha Surf ;-)PS Don't forget to pack your daily delivered newspaper to your room, in your luggage--I'm still reading my nine newspapers ;-)Aloha and Mahalo! ;-)

<Author>MisConMike
<Content>A comfortable stay First, a few particulars: I'm a 43 year-old male, making this (my first) Hawaii trip alone. I arrived late on a Sunday night to find that they had upgraded my standard room to one of their junior suites due to over-booking. They allowed me to retain this room for both nights of my stay, while charging me only for the standard room rate. Ahhh, Aloha at work already! Yes, even the junior suite was small, especially when compared to the other major hotel chains. And yes, the noise from the garbage trucks was clearly audible up on the 16th floor - but keep in mind that this is a common complaint that applies to nearly all of the non-beachfront hotels in Oahu! I found the hotel staff (receptionists, maintainance workers, and room attendants) to be quite friendly and helpful - they even suggested (local, inexpensive) places to shop to avoid being gouged. While my stay at the Aston Aloha Surf Hotel was brief - I was already booked into another hotel for the rest of my trip - *I* found it quite comfortable.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Rooms are small but ok for two people My husband and I stayed at the Aston Aloha Surf Hotel for 5 nights during Christmas week (Dec. 21-26) and found the hotel to be average. I had read some of the horrible and average ratings that had been posted earlier to this website and was not expecting something great about the hotel because of them and what I found is that it wasn't so bad. The way I look at it is that if you are an extremely picky person you will not like it, but if you are not so critical you will find it okay.The higher floor you get the better, we stayed on the 15th floor where the noise is not so loud up there but you can still hear music and noise from people partying all night. The music was not loud everyday during our stay, it was particularly louder during Christmas Eve and Christmas. I was not impressed with the continental breakfast and decided to skip it a few times. The beach is very close only 3 blocks from the hotel, the grocery store is next to the hotel and the Intl. Marketplace is about 4 blocks from the hotel so we didn't have to drive to get something from the store or to shop for souvenirs. There are many choices of places to eat around the hotel from sit down restaurants to fast food places. Overall this hotel was ok for the price.Aloha

The rooms were clean, however the kitchenette in the deluxe rooms are a joke! The countertop was peeling and very very small! The hotel staff were not one bit accomodating to our very late departure from Honolulu. We asked for a later checkout, but were told that we had to pay for an extra day if we wanted to have the room after 12p.m.Bottom line here is that you get what you pay for....

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Small but ok Stayed at the Aloha Surf Hotel in mid-November 2003 and it was ok. My room was clean but small. One other problem was that the air conditioner really did not work too well. Thank goodness it was peak summer.I'd recommend this hotel for the following types of travelers:1) College students who have some free time in the summer and want to get away without paying a lot of money. No frills come with this hotel, but for me, cleanliness is the most important thing, and this place has it (at least in my room). (This hotel is not within easy walking distance to the beach even though it is not geographically far from the ocean.) Staying at this hotel will allow the traveler to not spend a lot on lodgings and can put the money saved toward other things.-Mondetraveler

<Content>Never again! Me too! My Wife and I started our honeymoon in Oahu and found it to be anything but Island Paradise. This was our first trip to Hawaii and were planning on seeing paradise. But Waikiki was everything but paradise. So if you are looking for quiet away from every day city life stay out of the Honolulu area. The hotel staff was fabulous! But like most of the other reviews we have read here the rooms were not. The pool was a very sad site. It reminded us of the movie Vacation. It looked very dirty! Be prepaired, the view from any window in this hotel is going to be of high rise apartments with washers and dryers and hanging clothes from every single balcony as far as the eye can see. But if you look straight up you can see the beautiful blue sky. The walls outside the hotel on nearby buildings are ridden with graffiti. Yes it is close to the beach, 3 blocks. And many stores and restaurants close by as well. But every hotel has that. Our first room which we spent a whole 10 minutes in was so small that when we got our 4 bags of luggage in it we had to clime over the bed to get to the door! The bathroom was so small you could touch all 4 walls without even moving. We were lucky enough to get a 2 level upgrade. Unfortunately the room smelled like someone had a college party in it the night before! We went out and bought insensce to help. This wasn't something we even expected to have to deal with on our paradise honeymoon. But it was the only alternative and it was quite a bit bigger with a sofa area and small kitchenette equiped with a microwave and fridge. The staff was great and when they found out it was our honeymoon they sent up a bottle of Champagne and a box of Chocolate covered Macadamia nuts. This hotel was so bad we decided to leave the do not disturb sign on the door all day while we were out becuase we didn't want anyone touching our stuff. We may have been a little over paranoid but better safe than sorry. Thank God we were only there 2 nights. BEWARE!!! If a man walking on Waikiki beach asks you if you want your picture taken with his parrot. RUN! He assaulted me! Our first day in Paradise was not even close! But everything got much better after that day.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Great Stay Stayed at Aloha Surf September 15 to September 22, 2003. Room was small, but very clean. Staff was friendly and responded quickly to a problem I had with the safe. Parking is a problem. They only have 36 parking spaces and 200 rooms. Everytime we went somewhere, we did not know if we had a parking space or not. If no spaces are available at the Surf, you can park right next door in the Food Pantry parking lot. Fee is $7.00 if you park after 6:00PM. If you are looking for a clean room that does not cost much, then this is the right place for you. There are a few ladies of the night in the area, but they never presented a problem and I never did see one of the working girls around the Aloha Surf. I would stay at the Aloha Surf again. Very close to everything we wanted to do.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Aloha Surf...Made this surfer feel at home Spent 10 thru 18 Sept. at the Aloha Surf. Upon check in 2 hours early, was given a free room upgrade from a standard to deluxe without even asking. The room was on the 8th floor, and though small, had two double beds, and a futon(pull out bed). The bathroom and sink area were very clean, and the view from the lanai was beautiful. I was more than pleased with the room after reading some of the reviews on this hotel. The staff was friendly, and I drank the coffee supplied to my room every day, and didn't have to pay extra for it. The lobby was beautiful, and open aired, and the continental breakfast was OK. The best part of the trip was that everywhere we went the people remembered us from our last visit in March(see review Ohana East Hotel). For those coming to Hawaii in the near future, there is no city transportation att. The BUS is currently on strike and has been for over three weeks and there is no end to the strike in sight for the forseeable future, so if you come you better know the Hawaiian directions because there is no I repeat no North, South, East or West, nor will anyone use those words, and I will not give you the Hawaiian words. If you want to learn these words buy a Fodor's or Frommer's to learn them and I guarantee, with no bus transportation, you will definitely need to know them. I guarantee you will not want to use the Waikiki Trolley at 20 dollars a day, so you will be spending a great deal of time hoofing it (taxis are expensive). Because of no citywide transportation, we decided to to to the free breakfast sponsored by Aloha VIP tours. The breakfast was great and we learned that by attending this breakfast we were able to get substantial discounts on the tours that we took. My son won a free luau at Germaine's and I bought my ticket for the luau ( we weren't planning on going to the luau, but I am glad we did). The food and show were great and I would do it again. On Monday, we went on a 2 hour horseback tour of the Kualoa ranch (I won that ticket for two at the breakfast) and the tour was perfect, after that we took the 2 hour ATV tour of the ranch( I bought that tour because my son wanted to ride horses and since we won the horseback tour we did the ATV at the same time for the same price at the tour we won). Both tours took us to where they filmed Godzilla, Mighty Joe Young, George of the Jungle, Tears of the Sun, Jurassic Park and others, we even walked in Godzilla's footprints. On Tuesday we did another circle island tour, this one by Robert's tours of Hawaii, a reverse of the tour we took with E Noa in March. On Tuesday evening we participated in the Great Waikiki Beach Endless Summer 2003 Pub Crawl where we hit 24 nightclubs in 12 hours. It cost us 35 dollars each but each bar gave is one mixed drink ($4.50) or a beer, your choice. My son had 28 mixed drinks (rum and cokes and one 180 proof tequila and I had 40 mixed drinks 36 rum and cokes 3 blue hawaiis and one fuzzy navel). We started with 63 persons and at 4 in the morning when the crawl ended there were only me my son and two young females from Sacramento standing. The reason we were standing is our martial arts knowledge of the Dim Mac (presure points) which enabled us to move the alcohol from the drinks to various points of our bodies enabling us not to get drunk. My son won 50 dollars of a cop because he bet him that with what we drunk we would come in under the .08 that Hawaii uses to consider a person under the influence. I was .05 and my son was .03, and the amout of drinks we consumed was confirmed by our pub crawl cards that were punched at each pub stop. on Wednesday we took a hikeing tour in the Koolau range near the Pali lookout. The first tour was on the Hono side of the lookout and the 2nd was from the Koolau golf course just below the Pali Lookout to about 150 feet below the lookout a climb of about 1050 feet. I highly recommend this tour through Hawaii echo if you like hiking. We saw the Don Ho show again and it was outstanding, He didn't try to promote his kids as much as last time, but he did show Hoku's new video. He didn't sing one of his normal songs that he always does, and I mentioned this to him and he gave me and my son free tickets to see his show two nights later (Saturday the 13th) and I wound up singing that song along with another song on stage with Mr. Ho., plus receiving every CD that he ever did. We also continued to start our days at 4am by getting up, going to the beach where my son worked out, and I surfed before the beach got crowded, then going back to the hotel about 5:30 to change and eat breakfast and do what we wanted to do before 10. We also did some snorkeling at Hanauma Bay (highly recommended), and lots of shopping at Ala Moana and the IMP. With no bus I do not recommend going to Pearl unless you can get a tour to get you out there by 6:30 so you can get on the first couple of boats out (Good luck), or rent a car. If you get there much after 7, you will probably have a wait of at least 2 to 4 hours just to get a ticket for the boat. I am not trying to scare anyone from coming to the islands, but as I said at the beginning, with no bus transportation around the island, you will need to know the Hawaiian directions because they will not use N S E W nor can you get them to say those words. They also use those words on the news and for the weather reports, also be prepared for major traffic backups if you rent a car, no bus means everyone is driving to the city. Good luck on your trip to the islands and I hope this helps somebody out. The reason I mentioned Fodor's and Frommer's is because If you buy one of these books at least you will learn the directions and not get lost, and you will also learn a little about your hotel before you get there. Aloha and Mahalo Nui Loa  
<Date>Sep 23, 2003
